Special Letter from Beiping

Fengtai Travelogue 45

— Tang

Fengtai is a small town south of Beiping, belonging to the special municipality of Beiping, known throughout the Beiping-Tianjin area for its production of flowers, fruits, vegetables, and the like. Since the White Russian Mutiny, the "friendly nation's" troops have occupied warehouses, built barracks, and held endless exercises. This year, misunderstandings between Chinese and Japanese troops have repeatedly occurred, and the "September 18th" incident shook the entire nation when another misunderstanding between the two armies arose. Thus, this tiny town has become famous throughout the country under the name of the "nest of trouble." In reality, it is the throat between Beiping and Tianjin. Further west, all the way to the Lugou Bridge on the Beiping-Hankou Railway, it is part of the "friendly nation's" military stronghold. The railways passing through here include the Beining Railway and the branch line from Beiping to Lugou Bridge. Although the town is small, its strategic importance is extraordinary. After the "September 18th" incident was resolved, a part of our 19th Route Army garrison withdrew from the town; therefore, the local situation in the past ten days or so has become the focus of attention for a group of people in society.

Fengtai is about twenty kilometers, or forty Chinese li, from Zhengyangmen in Beiping. It takes half an hour by express train and more than two hours by slow train, which stops at four stations along the way. In order, they are Zhengyangmen in Beiping, Dongbiandou, Yongdingdou, and finally Fengtai. The reporter took the Beining Line No. 23 Pingyu express train from Zhengyangmen Station at 1:00 PM. The weather was fine and sunny along the way, and the sorghum swayed incessantly, a sea of ​​ocher-yellow as far as the eye could see. Occasionally, where the corners of houses and mud walls were exposed, there were always advertisements for Daxue Eye Drops, Lao Du Eye Drops, Ajinomoto, Wei Huo, Jintan, Zhongjiang Tang, Hongxing Partridge Vegetables, and the like. These advertisements are arranged in an exceptionally neat manner. Along the forty or fifty li from Zhengyangmen to Fengtai, various advertisements take turns appearing on the walls and corners of houses in the countryside, without overcrowding or omissions. It is conceivable that some kind of unified arrangement procedure has been gone through, which is not yet known. The area of ​​the advertisements is unusually large, entirely filling the entire wall surface, leaving no gaps. All the walls that can be seen from the train are plastered with them. For dozens of miles, what comes into view are rows and rows of what appear to be billboards with roofs, which can also be described as a spectacle.

This train has more than a dozen cars of first, second, and third class. The reporter inspected each car, and there were few passengers in the first and second class cars. Ten minutes after the train left the station, in the first-class dining car, the reporter witnessed a fat waiter in a white uniform dozing off at the table, drooling nearly three inches. This shows how idle and inactive they were. The third-class cars were crowded with passengers, but most of them were going to Tianjin and the Tangshan area. Only a few people planned to go to Shanhaiguan and then leave the pass to go to the puppet "Manchukuo." When the reporter spoke to one of them, the person was tight-lipped, holding his leather bag tightly, as if afraid of being questioned. There were three or five vagrants of a certain country, wearing cheap cloth suits without ties, walking back and forth in each car; the leather shoes without laces lazily dragged back and forth on the iron floor of the car, making a constant "ti ta" sound. Sometimes they would suddenly stop and stare at the passengers, as if paying close attention. But as soon as the passenger looked back at them, they would show an indifferent expression and wander away. Whether there was anything of note remains unclear, making people unsure what to believe. In the third-class car, there were a dozen or so lamas and dozens of Han people from the Wuchuan area of ​​Suiyuan Province, occupying a section of the car exclusively. The lamas were all wearing maroon robes, but they were very greasy. Each person held a string of prayer beads in their hand, muttering words. The Han people were all wearing blue cloth gowns, red-topped melon-skin hats, with long hair dragging three or four inches behind their heads. Those who occasionally took off their hats had their foreheads and tops of their heads shaved very cleanly, still in the style of the long braid era. It is conceivable that the long braids may have been recently cut off, which is not yet known. Of their speech, only a few simple words such as "Tianjin," "Wuchuan," and "Taiping" could be understood. However, from these simple words, it can be known that they came to Beiping from Wuchuan and were transferring to Tianjin. And the current situation in Wuchuan (the reporter notes that this place is an important route from eastern to western Suiyuan, and Wang Ying's bandits often traveled back and forth here) can be roughly known from the word "Taiping." As for their purpose in going to Tianjin, because communication was difficult, after many inquiries, it was impossible to find out the key point.

At 1:30 PM, the train arrived at Fengtai Station. The vagrants in the car also swarmed off the train here, and the reporter followed them. Fengtai is a small town. Apart from the area near the station, there are very few people in the town who are neatly dressed. Only vagrants of a certain country often stroll through the dilapidated streets in clumsy suits. Therefore, anyone wearing a suit who doesn't talk much is in danger of being suspected as a person from the "friendly nation." When the reporter walked through the streets, he felt that he was being stared at by passers-by everywhere. At first, he didn't know why, but after paying more attention, he realized that their eyes actually contained two kinds of meanings: fear and disgust. Having been suspected as a person from the "friendly nation," he felt a blockage in his heart, as if he had swallowed something greasy, an indescribable discomfort. But the vagrants seemed to look at me with the eyes of their own kind, which was completely different from the contemptuous and teasing gaze they gave to the local residents, which was quite ridiculous. But thinking about being in this "nest of trouble," without any guarantee, and at risk of being teased at any time, it is better to take advantage of this uncertain suspicion, which can make one feel slightly safer. Therefore, he remained silent and relied entirely on his eyes to make a rough observation of everything. In reality, even if he inquired in many ways, I am afraid that no one would dare to tell him the situation.

The street is about a li long, and signs of decline can be seen everywhere. The social order is superficially stable, but the suffocating air of being under some kind of heavy pressure can also be felt everywhere. The street is a north-south street, and the market is only on one side. The houses are not opposite each other across the street, but all face east, facing the station. In front of the street, there is a small ditch two or three feet wide, winding from south to north, with a length equal to that of the street. Dirty water flows gurglingly, and the sunlight evaporates, filling the air with stench. "Friendly nation" troops carrying weapons can be seen coming and going constantly. Outside the town, there is a faint sound of artillery and machine guns, intermittently transmitted. This is because that day happened to be the first day of a large-scale exercise. As for the gray uniforms of our country's army, I had seen one at the Shuidimen Station on this trip. As for the streets of Fengtai, they were even more invisible.

While walking through the streets, there was a sound of gongs and drums, coming from the south of the street and echoing the rumbling artillery and the staccato machine guns from afar. Following the sound, I suddenly saw a white cloth flag more than ten feet wide, flying horizontally in the air. From afar, I could clearly identify the large characters "Japan-China Joint Wufeng Grand Theater" on it. When I arrived at the door, I saw that two large Chinese national flags and a certain country's sun-shaped national flag were crossed and inserted on the door, which felt very incongruous. The so-called grand theater was just a tall shed made of mats. Three or five vagrants were lined up in front of the door, loudly soliciting passers-by. When the reporter arrived at the door, he hesitated slightly, but this had already attracted their special attention. Their eyes were shining and fixed on me without any rest, so it was better to make a decisive decision. He strode into the venue with a lofty and wide gait. At this time, they suddenly changed their previous attitude and did not ask the reporter for a ticket, only announcing after letting me pass, "Buy a ticket to see the show," "Buy a ticket to see the show." Even if I ignored them, I suppose they would not necessarily come to ask for it again. However, the reporter still took out a dime ticket, bought a ticket, and entered. When buying the ticket, I was also given a so-called "gift lucky draw ticket." According to its explanation, customers can choose any number from 1 to 40. At the end of the show, a lottery is held, and there is hope of winning a prize. At the back of the venue, there was a long table, and a red paper was posted on the wall, stating "Military and Police Control Seat." In front of it, sat a person wearing a Western-style autumn overcoat on top and Chinese-style cotton pants on the bottom, holding a civilization cane. Presumably, this person was the so-called "military police." This person sat and lay uneasily, constantly making teasing gestures to the customers. The reporter witnessed him hooking up the bound feet of an old woman from the countryside with the curved handle of his civilization cane. The old woman almost fell over, screamed in alarm, and quickly pulled her foot back. The person then quickly hooked the old woman's other foot with his cane, causing screams to continue. The person then clapped his hands and laughed. The seats in the venue were divided into male and female sections, separated by wooden fences. In each section, there were more than a hundred long wooden benches. Of the five or six hundred seats, there were surprisingly few empty ones, with three or four hundred people seated, which could not help but make me sigh. The customers were all from the lower classes of society. I really don't know where this one dime ticket came from. Was their purpose in coming here for entertainment, or solely for the lucky draw? And the ignorant and foolish state between their eyebrows, with a silly and silly smile, made me feel even more heartache when I saw it. On the stage, there were as many as five or six people playing instruments, and the singers were two children around ten years old. These two children would naturally make eye contact with the audience, which was extremely sad. The singing was shrill, like a chicken crowing, and it was impossible to tell what they were singing. Just as the reporter was raising his eyes to look around the venue, he suddenly heard a strange sound of "hao yi hao yi," which arose in a roar. He quickly looked at the stage and saw a female actor of fifteen or sixteen years old, coming out of the stage door, twisting and pinching as she walked towards the center of the stage. Two people, similar to railway workers, were whispering to each other at this time. One said: "Wow, look at that wave." The other said: "It's a pity she's lame." Thereupon, one of them loudly questioned: "Who said that?" The other also shouted loudly: "I saw it myself." The two argued endlessly, until they made a bet and went to the stage near the stage to see what was really going on. At this point, the reporter felt nauseous and could no longer bear it, so he left his seat and exited the venue, without seeing who won or lost.

Following the dirty and stinking ditch, I walked north along the street, intending to find a restaurant to eat and take the opportunity to see the situation, but I couldn't find one for a long time. When I reached the north end of the street, I finally saw a dilapidated restaurant. And next to it, there was a white wall with the words "Korean Cuisine" on it. I originally intended to go inside the white wall to see what it was like, but later, seeing a group of vagrants coming out from inside, I was afraid of causing trouble, so I stopped. After stepping into the dilapidated restaurant, flies swarmed and flew around, and there were no customers inside. But in a moment, I suddenly saw a person wearing a Western-style shirt with a tie on the upper body and khaki riding pants and black leather boots on the lower body, sharpening a pencil with a kitchen knife more than a foot long in front of the stove. The reporter chose a seat next to him, intending to see what was going on. On the table where this person was sitting, there was a bulging black leather bag, and in front of him was a notepad. He was not eating or drinking, but huddled in a corner, smoking a cigarette and pondering. Sometimes, he would scribble on the paper, not knowing what he was writing. When talking to the waiter, he was vague and difficult to understand, and mostly relied on gestures to help. This person was probably from the "friendly nation." I don't know what his mission was in lying here silently.

After leaving the restaurant, I continued north. When I was near the barracks of a certain country, I saw a dozen or so idlers standing on the side of the road. Two of them were arguing and wrestling. One side was a rickshaw puller, and the other side was a vagrant from a certain country. The vagrant was wearing a gray suit and punching the other person in the chest from time to time, muttering words in his mouth, not knowing what he was saying; but judging from his attitude and expression, it seemed to be vicious curses. The rickshaw puller stood still and took the blows, not daring to fight back. But as soon as the vagrant turned around to leave, he quickly grabbed the back collar of his suit and refused to let go, not caring about receiving even more violent punches as a result. According to the rickshaw puller, the matter they were arguing about was that when he stopped the rickshaw, a large copper coin fell out of his pocket and was picked up by the vagrant, who refused to return it. The rickshaw puller was old and simple, so what he said was probably true. After the vagrant tried to leave several times without success, he suddenly roared and pointed to the barracks that were close at hand, intending to drag the rickshaw puller inside. While they were wrestling, a team of young "friendly nation" soldiers returning from an exercise carried several machine guns back to the camp. Seeing this, the rickshaw puller quickly wiped his tears, picked up his rickshaw, and rushed away. The onlookers also scattered like birds and beasts. The vagrant strutted away triumphantly.

Around [time], the reporter returned to the station. After climbing onto the Beiping-Tianjin slow train, I finally felt a sense of relief and took a long breath. But when I saw the sun-shaped national flag of the "friendly nation" barracks erected high in the sky, I couldn't help but feel sorrow rising from within, and my chest felt bound. (September 28th.)

Page 5

Page 6

Current Affairs Commentary

The Significance of Japan's Control of the North China Paper Industry 46

Recently, Japanese paper industry capitalists, following the will of the military, have been preparing to establish large-scale paper mills in Tianjin, in an attempt to monopolize China's paper industry. The Toyo Paper Manufacturing Company plans to invest 10 million yuan to build a paper mill on the Haihe River in Tianjin Special Area and continue to establish branch factories in the five provinces of North China. Those responsible for the preparations are mostly important figures in the military. The Osaka Joint Paper Manufacturing Company has also purchased 3,000 mu of land in Dazhigu, Tianjin Special Area, with capital of 5 million yuan, to prepare for a paper mill. Japan's plan to develop the economy of North China is comprehensive, but the government uniquely recognizes the control of the paper industry as a major part of its national policy and must be implemented in advance, which has profound intentions. If this plan is completed, not only will China's paper industry, newspaper industry, publishing industry, and all cultural undertakings be greatly affected.

China's inability to be self-sufficient in paper production is the biggest weakness of the national economy. Although there are more than 30 small-scale paper mills in the country, their total capital is less than 10 million yuan and their annual output is only more than 400,000 pounds. Moreover, the quality is poor and insufficient for modern printing. Therefore, imports of foreign paper reach as high as 50 to 60 million yuan. If paper imports from Canada, Sweden, Norway, Japan, the United States, and other places are cut off, the domestic newspapers, publications, books, and official documents will inevitably come to a standstill. In recent years, the government and the people have deeply understood this crisis and are urgently seeking remedies. On the one hand, tariffs are used as a means to protect and promote the existing domestic paper industry, so that foreign paper prices are raised due to tariffs, and domestic paper can compete. On the other hand, large-scale paper mills are actively being planned as a fundamental solution. The Wenxi Paper Mill, with a capital of 4.5 million yuan, is a government-merchant joint venture company under preparation. Commercial shares of 600,000 yuan are borne by publishing merchants such as the Commercial Press, China, and Shen Bao News. Government shares of 3.9 million yuan are allocated from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity. The preparations for the factory are nearing completion, and machine purchases and factory construction are expected to be completed next year. Although its manufacturing quantity may only be enough for several newspapers in Shanghai, with this foundation, development will be easier.

Now, Japan is using its large capital, skilled and advanced technology and talents, and using the reeds of North China as raw materials, cheap labor, and its superior position in North China to establish paper mills to control the paper industry in North China and then control the entire Chinese paper industry. China's existing immature paper mills and the Wenxi Paper Mill, which is about to be completed, will inevitably suffer a great blow. Currently, Japanese paper, although there are imports of about 8 million yuan per year, is generally restricted by China's customs, with a tax of 2.6 gold units per 100 kilograms. The cost is high, and domestic paper can compete. Now, factories are established in North China, and the products are not subject to tariff restrictions. Domestic paper mills will lose their competitiveness, and the future of Wenxi Paper Mill is also very dim. China's paper industry will inevitably be controlled by Japan. Once an international war unfortunately occurs, the seaports are locked, and the source of paper from Sweden, Canada, the United States, and other places is cut off. Newspapers will have no way to publish, and the printing industry will completely stop. Then the whole country will enter a state of blindness, and the country can use its newspapers and leaflets to shake our people's hearts, frustrate our morale, and promote aggression as it pleases.

Therefore, we must not regard Japan's attempt to control the paper industry in North China as trivial. May the government authorities quickly plan the establishment of new-style paper mills and the development of existing paper mills, and quickly catch up to avoid digging a well when thirsty. The slightest bit of paper is actually related to national survival. We should pay attention to national defense work and should not only focus on airplanes and bombs.

Our Country Obtains Quasi-Permanent Council Seat General Assembly of the League of Nations Formally Approves Hungarian Representative Explains Stance on Armaments 47

(Geneva) The First Committee of the General Assembly of the League of Nations (i.e., the Committee on Legal and Regulatory Matters) previously passed a resolution on the 24th of last month, recommending to the General Assembly that the number of non-permanent Council members of the Administrative Council should be increased from nine to eleven. One of these seats should be given to China, and one seat should be retained by Portugal. The General Assembly of the League of Nations, meeting this morning, has definitely approved this resolution. Therefore, China's request to obtain a quasi-permanent Council seat has achieved its goal. (1st, Havas dispatch)

(Geneva) The General Assembly of the League of Nations continued its general debate on political issues at 10:00 AM this morning. Hungarian representative Tang Zuo Si delivered a speech, a key point of which was that even if the Third Committee of the General Assembly (i.e., the Committee on Disarmament Issues, which has been temporarily suspended due to the convening of the Disarmament Conference over the years, and the General Assembly this year has a motion to reorganize it) is re-established, Hungary will not be able to cooperate with it. (Tang Zuo Si's words may mean that Hungary intends to break away from the shackles of the Treaty of Trianon and reorganize its armaments.) Subsequently, Colombian representative Rocha No, Portuguese representative Hua Si Gong Sai Luo Si, representative of the Dominican Republic U Lai Na, Argentine representative Le Wei Lie, and Bolivian representative Ge Si Tai Du Ri Er spoke successively, discussing the issue of revising the Covenant of the League of Nations, all saying that the League of Nations should be inclusive of all countries in the world. The General Assembly then announced its adjournment and scheduled to continue the discussion tomorrow morning. (1st, Havas dispatch)

Spanish Rebel Leader Arrives at the Castle Franco Succeeds as Chairman of the Revolutionary Military Government General Labor Union Publishes Secret Agreement Between Rebels and Germany and Italy 48

Toledo General Franco, commander-in-chief of the rebel army, hurried here as soon as he received news of the rebel victory. According to what he said to people, "Relieving the siege of Al-Gazar is my lifelong ambition, and now the battle has indeed been won." When the general arrived here, he was greatly welcomed by the masses. As he drove into the city, everyone knelt on the left side of the road. He then got out of the car in front of the dilapidated castle. The women and children in the castle rushed out to kiss his hand. The scene when the general entered the castle was extremely moving. The castle has become a huge fortress of wood, stone, rough iron. The general cautiously walked forward to avoid touching the unexploded hand grenades scattered everywhere. Then he entered "Toledo's Black Hole," the dungeon in the castle. The dungeon was so dark that it was almost impossible to see things. There were still a hundred wounded lying on dirty curtains. The stench of rotten things was particularly unbearable. The general then went to congratulate the two mothers who had given birth in the siege. So he held a boy and stepped onto the ground, standing in the sunlight. This was the first time the child had seen the light since he was born. The general held the child up to show the crowd and shouted, "This is a symbol of Spain being saved after a fierce bloody battle!" (1st, Reuters dispatch)

Burgos General Franco, commander-in-chief of the National Army, was recently elected to succeed General Cabanellas as chairman of the military government. (1st, Havas dispatch)

Madrid The Spanish government today decided to implement a rationing system to avoid people gathering for long periods of time to get the amount of rice they need. At the same time, it will also take strict action to investigate the civil corps' requisition of civilian goods. These people constantly take by deception and force. For example, last week, they requisitioned 270 boxes of brandy from nine wine merchants, saying that they would be transported to the front line. After investigation by senior and middle-ranking officials, most of them were not transported to the front line. A week ago, eight British aviators were drinking freely in a fashionable wine shop in Madrid. Most of these people were temporarily in financial straits and were moved by high salaries to join the Spanish army and fight bravely for the government. Now none of them are left here. Three have died in battle, three have been seriously injured and are lying in the hospital, one is resting in Valencia, and the remaining one has gone to Paris. (1st, Reuters dispatch)

Madrid The organ of the National General Labor Union claimed that today it discovered a secret agreement between Italy, Germany, and the leaders of the Spanish rebels. Once the rebels are victorious, the three parties will share the spoils of war. It is said that the agreement has the following five understandings: (1) Germany will receive the Canary Islands. (2) Germany has the right to establish air and naval bases in the Pescadores Islands. Germany has already established a submarine base there. (3) Italy can get one of the Balearic Islands. (4) Germany will provide economic assistance and various privileges to Portugal and organize an anti-communist association in Portugal. (30th, Guomin dispatch)

Left-Wing Strong Men Defend the Capital Autumn Regular Meeting of the House of Representatives 49

Madrid Spanish strong men rose up to enlist today to assist the government. The roads and railways from Valencia to Madrid are crowded with vehicles, all carrying such strong men and food. Many residents of Madrid have joined the civilian corps and have begun training to defend the capital. (30th, Guomin dispatch)

Madrid Havas reporter special dispatch: Government troops have recently won a victory in Huesca Province in the northeast and have occupied Mount Aragon nearby. First Lord of the Admiralty Hoare Announces British Military Expansion Rate: Navy and Air Force Will Not Lag Behind, Powerful Strength Guarantees Peace, Conservative Party Supports Government Plan 59

(London) The Conservative Party held a conference today in the Maremma region. First, Sir Samuel Hoare, First Lord of the Admiralty, delivered a brilliant speech. The conference then passed a resolution supporting the government's national defense plan. Hoare's speech stated, in brief, that in this era of European rearmament, Britain has no other option but to implement rearmament without delay. The current situation is far worse than it was six months ago, when the government announced that major powers were increasing their armaments significantly. In the past six months, major powers have greatly increased their armaments, and even small countries such as Belgium, the Netherlands, and Switzerland are undertaking large-scale armament plans. There are two lessons that we should pay attention to: (1) the futility of unilateral disarmament; and (2) the necessity of greatly strengthening the British Empire so that it can become a force to safeguard peace. Germany's annual military expenditure is no less than 800 million pounds. The German budget, the army and navy departments, has reached an alarming 46 percent. Hoare also mentioned the rearmament situation in France, Russia, and the United States, saying that patriotic people should not ignore the armament figures of various countries. Current painful experience proves that the weakness of the British Empire is a factor in international political instability.

Hoare continued to describe the progress of British armaments, saying that the speed of the current naval construction program is quite beyond what was originally expected. The British Air Force has a large number of officers and soldiers with excellent performance, and new aircraft that can be deployed soon will not lag behind any country. Military supplies institutions were clearly exhausted in the years of the European War, and it may take some time to restore them. Britain has not yet reached the point where war arrangements are needed, and the recovery of economic prosperity will not be affected in any way. "From a broad national standpoint, I still believe that the wisest approach is to try to avoid this kind of enormous economic panic." Distorted pacifism and partisan views have had a considerable impact on army recruitment. The government should quickly take steps to inform the people more clearly about the needs of the country and the benefits of military service.

Hoare continued, saying that he would like to ask the responsible leaders of the Labour Party to assist in this effort, as they did during the European War. The government's armament plan is nothing more than the necessary part of Britain's obligations under the collective peace system or the maintenance of the lives and prosperity of a great people. Without the power of a great people, the world will fall into despair and chaos. Building fleets and expanding the air force are absolutely necessary and must be guaranteed. Strengthening the army and strengthening its strength are no less important. Any disarmament proposal that puts British armaments in a relatively weak position cannot be approved. If, as everyone hopes, a general disarmament can be negotiated, then it must be recognized that Britain's plan has been completed. In recent months, national defense has made definite progress, and the speed in the future will increase greatly. In 1936 alone, the program requires the construction of two battleships, seven cruisers, eighteen destroyers, two aircraft carriers, eight submarines, six small warships, and six motor torpedo boats. 80% of naval expenditure has been used in distressed areas, and the struggling shipyards have now resumed their activities. Fellow countrymen who have suffered are now regaining honorable work and fulfilling a part of their responsibility in the great national effort.

Hoare finally mentioned that Defense Minister Sir Thomas Inskip, Air Minister Viscount Swinton, and War Minister Cooper were attending meetings of the Imperial Defence Committee, so they were unable to attend today. (Reuters dispatch from London, 1st)

England-South Africa Air Race: Scott Wins Again, Flying 6,000 Miles in 53 Hours 60

Johannesburg Scott, the winner of the previous England-Australia Air Race, and Gutsly have won the Portsmouth to Johannesburg air race. Flying the same aircraft, they arrived at Germiston Aerodrome at 12:36 PM today, winning the prize of 4,000 pounds. This time, they flew 6,154 miles in 52 hours, 56 minutes, and 48.2 seconds, with an average speed of 123 miles per hour, reducing Mrs. Mollison's London to Cape air record by approximately 19 hours. If they decide to fly on, they can set a new record, but they have decided to stop here. A crowd initially gathered at the aerodrome and stayed up all night to welcome the winners, but due to the strong winds and sand in the morning, they returned home. Therefore, only 2,000 people remained when the winning aircraft arrived. The aircraft landed very smoothly. South African Defense Minister Bi Luo, the initiator of this competition, and South African industrialist Schlesinger, and Sir Melville, the first person to fly from England to South Africa, stepped forward to congratulate them. The obstacle competition winner has not yet been decided. At the time of the dispatch, Findlay and Waller's aircraft had left Khartoum at midnight and were between Anetebai and Bai Logan Mountain. Air Force officer Clauston is still in Khartoum repairing his aircraft's engine. It is reported that Loewin and Houston's aircraft were damaged near Lake Tanganyika, following Hails' aircraft. It is said that the two were looking for the Abercorn Aerodrome in Northern Rhodesia in the sky, but the fire on the grass field produced thick smoke, obscuring their vision. Due to running out of fuel, they landed and the aircraft was destroyed. However, when Scott and Gutsly's aircraft arrived in Abercorn, the smoke had cleared and they were able to land safely. Leaving Abercorn at 4:45 AM this morning, they could have arrived at the finish line at 11:00 AM, but they did not arrive until 12:36 PM. If Rue-Xiu II's aircraft had not been blinded by smoke, the outcome would have been difficult to determine. Now that this aircraft has been destroyed, Scott has the trophy in hand. Both showed no signs of fatigue after exiting the aircraft. An official carried Scott's luggage, and Scott followed him to the aerodrome office. Someone poured him a glass of beer, and just as Scott was about to drink it, a phone call came from London congratulating him on his success. Scott then talked for many minutes before enjoying the fragrant food and drink placed beside him. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

Now France, the Netherlands, and Switzerland are following suit. If major countries convene a meeting to discuss monetary stability, remove exchange and trade controls, develop a large-scale international bill exchange, and restore free credit understanding, Germany is also prepared to participate. If Germany's external debt can be reduced or abolished, Germany is also willing to abandon its monetary control. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

French New Monetary Law: Conflict Between Senate and Chamber of Deputies, Compromise Finally Reached, Article on Raising Prices Passes with a Compromise 63

(Paris) The Senate and the Chamber of Deputies conflicted over the new monetary law today because the Chamber of Deputies rejected the amendment passed by the Senate by a majority of 351 to 217 and passed the original bill again. The dispute intensified. The Chamber of Deputies has submitted the original bill to the Senate for reconsideration. The point of contention is that after the Senate passed the franc devaluation bill, it deleted the clause granting Prime Minister Blum full power to prohibit raising prices. The Chamber of Deputies insisted on the original bill. The reason why the Senate was dissatisfied with the bill was that it contained socialist elements and feared that it would grant the government dictatorial powers. (National Telegram dispatch from Paris, 30th)

(Paris) Regarding the new monetary law proposed by the government, the Chamber of Deputies re-voted and passed the original bill last night, and rejected the amendment proposed by the Senate. The Senate Finance Committee re-examined it this morning, and formulated a compromise plan. The Senate then passed it by a show of hands at 1:30 PM today. According to the compromise plan, if the standard of living increases due to currency devaluation, causing social disputes, the government can use compulsory arbitration to resolve it, but only after consulting the National Economic Council in advance. The Chamber of Deputies is scheduled to meet again at 2:30 PM to submit the compromise plan for a vote. In addition, although the method of compensating veteran pensions was specified in Article 16 of the original bill, the Senate rejected it at its meeting yesterday, believing that this compensation method should not be included in the monetary law. If a separate bill is proposed, it can be approved. Therefore, the government has already drafted another bill and submitted it to the Finance Committee of the Chamber of Deputies. It is expected that the committee can pass it, so that the Chamber of Deputies can submit it for a vote at its afternoon meeting and send it to the Senate for review. People in the Deputies' lounge recently said that after several back-and-forth discussions between the Senate and the Chamber of Deputies this afternoon, the new monetary law can be finally passed. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

(Paris) The Finance Committee of the Chamber of Deputies convened at 2:30 PM and passed the compromise plan proposed by the Senate regarding the new monetary law. The point of contention between the Senate and the Chamber of Deputies can be said to have been resolved, so the entire new monetary law can be established tonight. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

Senate Amendment 64

(Paris) The Senate discussed the monetary law all day. After intense debate, it finally held a vote at 9:40 PM tonight, passing the entire bill by a majority of 141 votes to 125. However, the section in the original bill passed by the Chamber of Deputies, which "grants the government full power to prevent price increases," was deleted, and replaced with another section stipulating that "the government only has the right to prohibit price increases when there is no legitimate reason." Before voting on the entire bill, it was submitted for a vote article by article. When Article 1 of the original bill, which stipulated "repealing the monetary law of June 25, 1928," was submitted for a vote, it was only passed by a majority of 137 votes to 127. In other words, the government only had a majority of ten votes. During the Senate debate this afternoon, senators from the centrist and right-wing factions spoke out one after another, attacking the government, saying that since the People's Front government came to power, its authority has been lost, and it has even condoned workers who occupy factories because their demands for wage increases have not been met. As a result, the devaluation of the franc is the inevitable result of the government's mismanagement. Finance Minister Olivier refuted them separately, saying that "currency devaluation is the result of the general international economic situation. For six years, countries around the world have been devaluing their currencies due to the recession. Only France, under previous governments, has always adhered to the policy of currency tightening and did not know how to adapt. Until other countries successively broke away from the bondage of the currency system and gradually recovered prosperity, only France was trapped in a golden cage and could not escape. Why is this so? France's gold reserves at the beginning of 1935 were still 90 billion francs, but later suddenly decreased to 54 billion francs, and it is impossible to allow it to continue to flow out. As for thinking that prices will inevitably skyrocket after the devaluation of the franc, this is also an overestimation, because currency devaluation and inflation are different. Inflation will inevitably raise prices, while currency devaluation will not affect domestic trade."

Former Finance Minister Caillaux then spoke, "In principle, I do not oppose the devaluation of the franc, but the losses from devaluation should be borne jointly by people of all classes. It is absolutely impossible to allow one class of people to exclusively benefit from the devaluation, while the middle class and those who live on interest bear the entire loss of the franc devaluation... Furthermore, it is a mistake to think that increasing purchasing power can solve the economic panic, because France is an agricultural country, and the suffering it is now experiencing is due to overproduction in industry, not due to insufficient purchasing power." Finally, Prime Minister Léon Blum delivered a speech to answer the opposition party's various criticisms of the government's social policies, saying, "I firmly believe that my task is to seek universal harmony and appeasement. I am confident that I will achieve this goal, but it cannot be achieved by means of mutual retaliation, because the result of mutual retaliation will inevitably lead to a real social war. When Congress adjourned in August of this year, the national strike wave had almost disappeared, but it rose again in September, but now it has returned to calm. As for whether the government's monetary policy can be successful, it depends entirely on whether employers and employees can trust each other. Even if there are occasional labor disputes, they should not be deliberately exaggerated to create hostile propaganda. We must continue to fulfill our responsibilities in the future and use persuasion and mediation to quell all labor unrest." Finally, Prime Minister Léon Blum declared that the Senate had amended the section in the original bill passed by the Chamber of Deputies regarding the prohibition of price increases, and the government could not assume responsibility for it, because "a moment ago I asked you to find a way to allow the government to avoid future social conflicts, but now you insist on causing a conflict between the Senate and the Chamber of Deputies, which is not what I want."

However, the Senate finally passed the monetary law in accordance with the Finance Committee's amendment, and deleted the section authorizing the government to prohibit price increases. The Senate is scheduled to meet again at 9:30 AM tomorrow. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

Chamber of Deputies Insists 65

(Paris) After the new monetary law was amended and passed by the Senate, it should be returned to the Chamber of Deputies for reconsideration according to law. The Chamber of Deputies convened at 11:26 PM last night. Chairman and Speaker Herriot, as well as Finance Committee rapporteur Schmid and representatives of various left-wing parties, presented reports, advocating that the original Article 14 of the bill, which the Senate had deleted, that is, "granting the government full power to prevent price increases," be changed to Article 13B, "the government only has the right to prohibit price increases when there is no legitimate reason," and should be rejected. The deputies then began to debate. Several right-wing deputies fiercely attacked the devaluation of the franc and criticized the government's bill for not proposing compensation measures for farmers. Finance Minister Olivier stood up and replied that, according to the agreement reached between the United Kingdom, the United States, and France, the French stock exchanges should reopen tomorrow, and asked the Chamber of Deputies to vote quickly. When the vote was held at 1:35 AM this morning, the original bill of the Chamber of Deputies was passed again, and the clauses deleted by the Senate were rejected. In addition, Article 25 "B" was passed and listed at the end of the original bill, with the following text: "Those who have engaged in spot or futures trading on domestic securities exchanges or commodity exchanges before the currency devaluation order on the 26th of last month and have made a profit shall be levied a special tax of 50% on the amount of profit earned at the time of this month's settlement. This special tax shall be deducted by the brokers from their customers and submitted to the government." The entire bill has now been returned to the Senate for reconsideration, and the Senate is scheduled to meet at 9:30 AM today to discuss it. According to predictions from political circles, if the Senate does not change its attitude at that time, the government is in danger of collapsing when it finally proposes a vote of confidence, which will inevitably cause extremely serious disputes in politics and society. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

Rural Relief in Luxi: Organizing Financial Circulation Offices to Handle Loans, Remittances, Deposits, and Warehousing 67

Jinan Communication: In recent years, rural bankruptcy and economic panic have affected the market, financial activity is stagnant, and industry and commerce are gradually becoming depressed. The Luxi area suffered a particularly severe flood last year, making the rural situation even more difficult. The Second Administrative Inspectorate of Heze, in view of this, and in order to seek relief, recently established financial circulation offices in its subordinate counties to handle loans, remittances, deposits, loans, and warehousing, etc., to regulate rural finance. A joint office of financial circulation offices was also established in the second administrative region of Heze to comprehensively manage all matters in the counties. Lai Zhizhong, director of the joint office, came to Jinan a few days ago to contact major banks for loans and remittances. He completed his affairs this morning (27th) and returned to Heze by car. The following is a record of his conversation:

According to Lai, the method of relieving the rural areas is that this district is responsible for the establishment of financial circulation offices in each county to relieve rural bankruptcy. A joint office of financial circulation offices was also established in Heze. The six counties of Heze, Dingtao, Chengwu, Shanxian, Yuncheng, and Jinxiang have been established and officially opened on September 10. Each uses the surplus of local funds from previous years as a fund. The surplus of each county is 20,000 to 30,000 yuan for the smaller ones, and 70,000 to 80,000 yuan for the larger ones, with a total of more than 200,000 yuan already raised as a fund. As for the scope of business, it is roughly divided into (1) loans. The main business of the office is rural loans, most of which are lent to cooperatives to be distributed to farmers at low interest. The second is short-term mortgage loans, which are lent to commercial firms. (2) Deposits, to collect idle funds from the community, and store them for long and short terms. An account can be opened with one yuan. Because most counties do not have banks, depositors are very enthusiastic. (3) Remittances. In addition to counties with circulation offices responsible for mutual remittances, they have also contacted a major bank in Jinan to be responsible for handling remittances to various counties in Luxi inside and outside the province. The stipulated remittance rate is extremely low. This contract can be established soon. (4) Exchange. Since the implementation of the legal currency, silver has no longer circulated in the market. Merchants are very picky about banknotes, and damaged ones are rejected. Farmers feel quite painful, so the office exchanges small amounts for them, and then brings them to Jinan to exchange for new banknotes. (5) In addition to local small loans provided by the financial circulation office, if there are large loans, the office will contact major banks to provide them. (6) Warehousing. The Heze Mutual Aid Society obtained a triple profit from running a bean warehouse in the 22nd year of the Republic of China. This year's soybeans, except for a small part affected by insect pests, have generally had a bumper harvest. The credit cooperatives are responsible for this business. The county government ordered the township agricultural schools in each county to prepare 30 to 50 warehouses, which are now ready. The number of self-produced soybeans that members are willing to store has been registered, and the registered number has reached 10 million catties. The county government should provide a part of the cash, which requires 300,000 yuan, and has now reached an agreement with a major bank in Jinan, and the contract will be signed soon. This warehousing method can be started after it is approved by the provincial government.

Cotton Society Seeks Members

The Jiangsu Taijiaobao Cotton Production and Marketing Cooperative, a limited liability company, agreed with Liuhe Yaodesheng, Yongyi, and Dachanghe Flower Firm on the 23rd of last month that those who sell flowers with the cooperative's flower selling certificate will be given an additional yuan per dan based on the market price. All rights and obligations are exactly the same as those of formal members.

Wuxi 70

Stage Collapse Injures People

Zhang Zhonghou, the owner of Dacheng Silk Factory in Longchuanhong outside the west gate of this town, hired the Zhejiang Central Grand Stage Opera Troupe organized by Hu Chenglin to perform operas to thank the gods in the open space next to the factory during the Mid-Autumn Festival because the factory's grand immortals were causing trouble. The gong was struck at 2 pm, and at about 3 pm, when the stage was performing the scene of Cheng Jingsi and Jie Bao from Pearl Curtain Peak, Li Keyong refused to send troops, the stage suddenly shook, and with a crash, the front and back stages all collapsed. The audience scrambled to escape, and the order was disrupted. At that time, Jiangbei children Ren Genbao (14 years old), Koubao (10 years old), and Koudi (4 years old) were crushed, as well as Hu Xu, who set up a lotus root stall, and onlookers Zhang Xinru and Zhu Pangeng, etc., were all bleeding from their heads, and the situation was very tragic. Among them, Ren Genbao was the most seriously injured because he was injured in the chest, and his life may be in danger. All were sent to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. The Central Stage also suffered considerable losses, with all the boxes, cages, and clothes crushed. All the actors fell off the stage and suffered minor injuries. The responsible Public Security Fourth Branch immediately sent a police officer to investigate and handle the matter.

Changzhou 71

Water Thieves Confess to Robbery

At 6 pm on the 29th of last month, the Public Security First Sub-Bureau outside the west gate of Wuyi, together with the patrol team outside the west circle gate, successively captured seven stolen boats and eight thieves, including Sha Shoushan, and several pieces of stolen goods such as rice, wheat, clothing, and bedding in the river. They confessed to stealing from warehouses and other places in the city. On the 30th, patrol officer Zhou Daonan rigorously interrogated them again. The criminals then confessed that on the evening of the 14th of last month, they robbed the house of Sheng Linhai at Magong Bridge in Ximen, and divided the stolen goods for use. They also confessed that there was a fake pistol that was thrown into the river before being arrested. Patrol Officer Zhou sent police to retrieve the fake pistol but failed. He immediately summoned the colleague, who confirmed that it was the original stolen item. Because the thieves were actually a large group of water bandits, it was assumed that they had robbed other places, so they were still being rigorously interrogated and will be sent to the court for trial within a few days.

Danyang 72

Epidemic Spreads in Erling

In the southwest townships of this town, malignant malaria is extremely rampant and has now spread to the Erling area in the east. Most people who contract malignant malaria die. It is now heard that the doctors and pharmacies in the town are all making three times the profit, and the coffins are also sold out, which shows that the spread of the epidemic is out of control. It is hoped that those responsible for the locality will provide relief as soon as possible to avoid the spread.

Chief of Public Security Bureau Changes

Cai Hongfan, the chief of the Public Security Bureau of this town, has now been transferred to Taixian by provincial order, and Zhang Funong has been appointed to fill the vacancy. The new Chief Zhang arrived in Dan yesterday and met with Chief Cai to discuss handover matters. He is scheduled to take office on the 30th. Chief Cai will take a car to the province on the afternoon of the 29th and transfer to Tai. As for the handover, it will be handled by Section Chief Wu De'en.

Zhenjiang 73

Opening of Koutai Highway

The Koutai Highway from Longwokou to Nandou section of Taixian, a total of 24 kilometers, has been completed for all roadbed and bridge culvert projects. The highway project office borrowed a car from the Yangjing Highway two days ago for two test runs, and the results were quite good. The road passes through the towns of Kouan, Diajiapu, and Sixiangkou, and reaches the south gate of Taixian. Many merchants and residents went to watch. It will soon be officially opened for passenger vehicles.

Yangzhou 74

Monk Gets on Bed, Young Woman Shows Power

Yao Jinjian's brother Jinwen, a resident of Guyin Temple Lane in Yangzhou, once shaved his head to become a monk and has always suffered from nerves. Yesterday, Jinjian's mother-in-law, Feng, brought her daughter-in-law to Yangzhou and stayed at Yao's house. This morning (30th), Yao Jinwen saw that Feng had gotten up, but his daughter-in-law was still lying down. He rashly got on the bed and lay down next to her. The daughter-in-law woke up in shock and slapped him in the face in anger. Then she took the door bolt and beat Jinwen on the head, causing him to bleed all over his face. Yao then cried out loudly, and the family gathered to mediate, and the storm subsided.

Huai'an 75

Fire Kills Three People

Zhou Lianjia's family, who lives next to Mingji Company on Ximen Street in this city, makes a living by making clothes. In addition to Lianjia, his family also includes his old wife Liang, a deaf-mute son Yunhong, and a daughter-in-law Wang, a total of five people. On the 25th, a car rented by a Li family from the north gate to pick up a bride was rented from Huaiyin Mingji Automobile Company. Because there was no gasoline, the driver Gao Changjiang drove to the north gate Mingji Company to add gasoline. Accidentally, it dripped onto the stove fire, and the entire house was burned down, spreading to Zhou Lianjia's clothing store, causing Lianjia, his wife, and his son Yunhong to be unable to escape and died in the fire. Zhou's daughter-in-law Wang and her two grandchildren were watching a play in the theater and were fortunate to escape. After the incident, the county government detained the driver Gao Changjiang and Wu Guisheng, the manager of Huai'an Mingji Company. As for the three Zhou family members who were burned to death, Mingji Company prepared coffins for burial.

Haizhou 76

Hailstorm Disaster in Weiqian Township

Weiqian and Weizhong townships in the first district of Guanyun County, which are six or seven li wide and more than ten li long, suddenly changed weather the day before yesterday. The wind was very strong, red clouds were densely distributed, lightning and thunder were intertwined, and hailstones suddenly fell, as large as chicken eggs and as small as chestnuts. It stopped after about ten minutes. The farmers in the township suffered this natural disaster and cried out in pain.

Apricot Trees Bloom

Zhang Caichen, a resident of Xiaohouzhuang, the fifth household in the first Jia of the seventh Bao in Nangang Township in the second district of this town, has an apricot tree planted for more than five years. Due to the mild climate, the tree suddenly bloomed with flowers all over the branches the day before yesterday, a mass of silver. In recent days, residents in the vicinity have heard the news and come to watch, and the road has been blocked. The generally superstitious villagers all believe that it is an auspicious omen for Zhang's family.

Shaoxing 77

Accident on Xiaoshao Road

At about 8 am on September 30th, a Xiaoshao section car, a car that traveled from Xiaoshan Jiangbian Station to Xinchang, carried more than a dozen passengers, driven by driver Guo Zhiquan, and drove to Taiping Bridge near Ruanshe Station. A woman named Sheng Mao from Tinghou Township happened to be coming towards them. The car honked its horn continuously, but the woman was foolish and ran around, so that the car and the person could not avoid each other, causing the woman to be hit. The car also overturned into the field and crashed into the tomb opposite. The entire body of the car was destroyed. All the passengers except one were unharmed, and the rest were seriously injured. Afterwards, the Shaoxing Station sent a car to send the injured Gao Yantong, Qian Zhongde, Pan Jiongxuan, Qiu Axin, Fan Shuchang, Chen Wen'e, Xu Qian, Zhao Shengcai, and the Chen couple to the Nanjie Fukang Hospital for treatment.

Several Famous International Cases of Protecting Overseas Chinese 78

— Li Shengwu

I. Introduction

On August 24th of this year, a mob riot occurred in Chengdu, destroying hostels and shops. At the time, there were casualties among soldiers, police, and civilians, and four Japanese residents in Sichuan were also beaten, two of whom, Watanabe Kōzaburō and Fukagawa Keiji, died of serious injuries. Takeo Tanaka and Hisashi Seto were rescued. After the case occurred, the local authorities immediately arrested two rioters and executed them on the spot. Japan sent warships to Chongqing, but the official negotiations between the two countries on this incident had not yet begun as of the time of writing. Unexpectedly, one wave has not yet subsided, and another wave has risen. Suddenly, newspapers on September 8th reported that Nakano Junzō, a local Japanese resident in Beihai, Guangxi, was killed during a demonstration (some say he died in a fight with a Chinese person). The details of this case are still unknown, and the official investigation report on the Chengdu incident has not been published. Under these circumstances, rashly commenting may inevitably lead to inaccuracies; not criticizing and merely placing various expectations on Japan's resolution of this case will not help the actual situation. Therefore, I will briefly describe several famous international cases of protecting overseas Chinese, in order to clarify the different ways in which such cases are resolved internationally. Secondly, I will also briefly discuss the responsibilities that a country should bear for harm to foreign residents.

The term "protecting overseas Chinese" has a broad scope. When a country's people reside in other countries, from being humiliated to having their lives and property harmed, and do not receive adequate protection from the government of the host country, or do not receive adequate remedy from the government of the host country after the incident, and are deemed to be contrary to fairness and justice, the government of the victimized overseas Chinese's home country has the right to rise up and protect them through diplomatic means. The records of international cases of protecting overseas Chinese are extremely numerous, and the circumstances of their occurrence are also extremely complex. This article only focuses on riot events, selects the key points for description, and also discusses in principle the events of harm to foreign residents that occur in countries during times of turmoil.

II. The New Orleans Mob Riot of 1891

On March 14, 1891, eleven Italian residents in New Orleans, USA, were brutally killed by a local mob on suspicion of assassinating Police Chief Hennessey (D.C. Heunesy). When the Italian residents were arrested, they were all arrested and imprisoned on suspicion of murder. Among them, five had not yet been tried, three had already been released, and the other three were awaiting second trial. As for the reason why Police Chief Hennessey was killed, it was because he tried to destroy a secret organization (called Mafia) and aroused hatred. After the eleven Italians were killed, the Italian consul in New Orleans immediately reported to the Italian Minister to the United States, who also received instructions from his country's Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the same day, requesting the US government to take swift and effective measures to protect the Italian people residing in New Orleans and to punish the rioters according to law. The Italian Minister, in accordance with these instructions, immediately prepared a document notifying the US government, while reserving the Italian government's right to claim compensation. On the same day, the US State Department telegraphed the governor of the location where the incident occurred (Governor Nicholls), placing the rioters under legal control and strictly preventing the occurrence of similar incidents. It also explained that the US-Italian treaty stipulated that the United States had the obligation to protect the lives and property of Italian residents, and the US President expressed deep regret for the occurrence of the New Orleans riot.

The US State Department sent a copy of the telegram to the Governor to the Italian Minister. However, the Italian government insisted on demanding compensation, and if this could not be done, it would withdraw its Minister to the United States. On March 31, 1891, the Italian Minister made the following two requests to the United States: (1) The federal government formally promised to punish the rioters. (2) In principle, recognize the right to compensation for the families of the victims. At the same time, it notified the US government that it would leave the US and return home immediately. After the Italian Minister returned home, the affairs of the Italian Embassy were taken over by the Chargé d'Affaires. On April 1, 1891, the US State Department's document to the Italian Chargé d'Affaires mentioned the above two requests, stating that the US government had recognized in principle the compensation for the victimized Italians, because their treaty rights in the US were infringed. However, the unfortunate incident that occurred on March 14th must be thoroughly investigated and should not be rushed excessively. Before formally agreeing to any request, the facts obtained from the investigation must be judged in detail according to law. This has been repeatedly explained to the Italian Minister who returned home. The Italian side's impatience may be understandable, but excessive impatience will not necessarily lead to a just resolution.

The Italian government misinterpreted the above document from the US government, believing that the US government formally recognized its responsibility for compensation. US Secretary of State Mr. Blaine then issued a note to the Italian Chargé d'Affaires on April 14, 1891, correcting his erroneous interpretation, and stating that the US President still had many facts to determine whether Italy's treaty rights had been infringed. After analyzing and discussing the various facts according to law, Blaine had the following sentence at the end of the document:

The Italian people who were victimized in the New Orleans riot were either temporary or long-term residents in the area. If their lives and actions were not contrary to the provisions of the US-Italian treaty, did not violate our country's immigration laws, did not hinder the public order of the United States, and complied with the laws of the United States and the places where the Italian residents lived, and if the government officials did not fulfill their responsibility to protect the lives and property of foreign residents, or condoned the occurrence of riots, or were aware of the crisis of riots and did not take appropriate deterrent measures, or did not bring the rioters to justice after the riots occurred. Under these circumstances, the US President will of course recognize that the case has been established and will submit it to Congress for consideration and provide relief to the relatives of the victims who were brutally killed.

On May 5, 1891, the Chief Justice of New Orleans prepared a report on the riot and pardoned the participants in the riot who attacked the prison. No charges were filed, and no trials were held.

On December 6 of the year following the riot, US President Harison made the following statement in his document to Congress:

The US government, in order to express friendship to the Italian government, deeply condemned the occurrence of the New Orleans incident and provided 125,000 francs as compensation. The King of Italy expressed his gratitude upon accepting it. The resolution of this case has greatly enhanced the friendly and mutually respectful sentiments between the US and Italy.

When US Secretary of State Blaine handed over the compensation of 125,000 francs to the Italian Chargé d'Affaires on April 12, 1892, he reiterated in the note that the damage suffered by the Italian people was not directly inflicted by the United States. In other words, the US government had no legal responsibility for this incident; however, the US President believed that paying satisfactory compensation was the sacred obligation and supreme pleasure of the US government. Blaine further stated that the US President hoped that the resolution of this case would be sufficient to dispel the negative impression caused by the case, restore the former friendly relations between the US and Italy, and prevent the occurrence of unfortunate incidents that could harm the harmony and sincerity between the two countries in the future. The Italian Chargé d'Affaires immediately accepted the compensation and replied to Blaine's words on behalf of the Italian government, while declaring in accordance with the instructions of the Italian government that the relations between the two countries were immediately restored from then on.

Looking at the resolution process of the New Orleans riot, two points are worth noting: (1) Italy's request to punish the murderers was not accepted by the US government. (2) The US government's compensation of 125,000 francs was an expression of friendship, not the fulfillment of legal responsibility. The 1885 massacre of overseas Chinese in Rock Springs, USA, is also worth mentioning. (To be continued)
