Local News

Income Tax Collection Begins Yesterday; Interest Income Tax on Deposits Postponed; Liang Jingchun Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning to Preside 79

Central News Agency reports: The Ministry of Finance is implementing income tax, initially collecting three types: second-class income from salaries and remuneration of civil servants, and third-class income from securities and interest on deposits. The announcement was made yesterday, but due to the delayed distribution of forms for the third-class interest on deposits, nationwide implementation could not occur simultaneously. The Ministry of Finance is considering alternative solutions. The details are as follows:

Ministry of Finance Proclamation

The Ministry of Finance issued a public announcement yesterday stating: It has been determined by the National Government that the income tax on salaries and remuneration of civil servants, as well as interest on government bonds and deposits, will be levied starting October 1, 25th year of the Republic. The important matters are announced as follows: 1. Tax Rates: Income from salaries and remuneration of civil servants will be taxed according to Article 5 of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations, calculated separately. Income from government bonds and interest on deposits will be taxed according to Article 6 of the same regulations. 2. Withholding: Income tax on salaries and remuneration of civil servants will be withheld monthly by the heads of the agencies directly paying the salaries. Income tax on government bonds and interest on deposits will be withheld by the responsible personnel of the paying institutions when reporting interest settlements. 3. Payment: Withholding agencies shall remit the withheld tax to the Central Bank or its designated agents, such as the Bank of Communications, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, or other tax collecting agencies, and obtain receipts. Separate orders will be issued for implementation. This announcement is issued by Minister Kong Xiangxi, September, 25th year of the Republic of China.

Ministry of Finance Response

The Shanghai Banking Association previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance, earnestly requesting a delay in the collection of income tax on third-class deposit interest income. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance responded, acknowledging the veracity of the request and demonstrating consideration by postponing implementation until January 1, 26th year of the Republic. However, the income tax on interest from government bonds will still be collected starting October 1. The original response is recorded below: The submission has been noted. The implementation date for the income tax on deposit interest has been announced. The collection methods are detailed in the Provisional Regulations and Implementation Rules. As for the flight of capital, since the announcement of the Income Tax Regulations, people from all walks of life have considered it a good tax system, demonstrating patriotism. Furthermore, the tax rates are very low. It is unlikely that people would violate their patriotic intentions to avoid paying taxes. In recent years, various countries around the world have either devalued their currencies or increased the amount of currency in circulation. Currency values ​​change from morning to evening, making it difficult to determine the definite standard for property prices. Only a foolish person would deposit their assets in foreign banks while residing in China, as they would not be able to understand the operating conditions and profit and loss situation. People should be able to recall the pain suffered by the Chinese in the past. Why would anyone risk danger and cause themselves trouble to avoid paying a small amount of tax? Even if there are a few who are unwilling to pay taxes and try to evade funds, the government will enforce the law without leniency. The original submission is excessive. However, the claim that this is a new undertaking, with complicated procedures and a tight schedule, making preparations extremely difficult, is true. Therefore, in order to show special consideration, the implementation date for the income tax on this item of deposit interest is temporarily postponed to January 1, 26th year of the Republic. However, the income tax on interest from government bonds should still be collected from October 1 as originally scheduled. In addition to the ministry submitting a report to the Executive Yuan for submission to the National Government for review and record, you should forward this to all fellow traders, and instruct each branch to follow and implement this together. This is of utmost importance. This order.

Liang's Remarks

The Income Tax Affairs Office was established in Nanjing yesterday, with Gao Bingfang and Liang Jingchun, the Director and Deputy Director of the Preparatory Office, respectively, in charge. Its structure is very simple. According to Deputy Director Liang, who arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning, the implementation of income tax has been supported by the whole country, and it is fortunate that it can be held as scheduled. The second and third classes have already been distributed by the Ministry of Finance to various agencies, and letters have been sent to various banks and money houses to withhold the tax. The procedures are simple, so the organizational structure of the Affairs Office does not need to be expanded. Staff will be dispatched to various provinces and cities to provide instructions. The establishment of branch offices in various locations is currently under consideration. In remote provinces and cities, locations in the commercial and industrial centers may be considered for establishment. As for the forms and receipts used for taxation, they have been sent out separately. Because the banking industry in this city received the forms and was unable to distribute them to various branches before the start of collection, Kong the Minister of Finance has considered the fact that institutions such as the Postal Remittance Bureau and Bank of Communications have dozens of branches and hundreds of sub-branches, and has decided to set another date for collection in order to ensure the consistency of taxation. The Ministry of Finance is determined to implement this decision in order to cultivate a good source of tax revenue and does not want to be hasty. The banking industry takes this seriously and studies it in detail. The government expresses its admiration and hopes to have a good contribution to make the procedures even more perfect, he said.

Order from the Ministry of Finance

New Voice News Agency reports: The Shanghai Banking and Money Trades Association received a directive from the Ministry of Finance the night before last, stating, "The Provisional Income Tax Regulations have been ordered by the National Government to be implemented from October 1, 25th year of the Republic, and it has been stipulated that the income from salaries and remuneration of second-class civil servants and the income from government bonds and interest on third-class deposits will be levied starting from October 1, 25th year of the Republic. All other incomes of the first, second, and third classes will be levied starting from January 1, 26th year of the Republic. Obey and follow the order. The records are on file. According to Article 18 of the regulations, those who are required to withhold income tax for third-class income should report the income amount in the prescribed format to the competent collection agency one month after paying the interest. Furthermore, the method of paying income tax stipulated in Article 27 of the Implementing Rules, which belongs to the third class, shall be withheld by the business person in charge of the interest-paying agency. The collection of income from the salaries and remuneration of second-class civil servants and the income from government bonds and interest on third-class deposits is imminent, and should be communicated to all and followed. In addition to the income tax on salaries and remuneration of second-class civil servants and the income tax on interest on third-class government bonds, which have been distributed separately by the Ministry for implementation, all income tax on deposit interest should be deducted in full by banks, money houses, silver companies, trust companies, savings societies, and money shops in various places, according to regulations, and those with taxes less than one cent should be rounded up or down. The collected taxes should be handed over to the local Central Bank or its designated tax collecting agencies, and remitted to the national treasury for collection. Furthermore, this income tax will be levied from October 1, 25th year of the Republic, and the interest income before October 1 will still be paid in full and exempted from deduction. The 'Collection Instructions for Income Tax on Third-Class Securities Deposit Interest' and the 'Report Form for Income Tax Amount of Third-Class Category D' are hereby attached, one hundred copies each, for compliance and for forwarding to all members of the same industry for compliance. As for those who are not members of the association, and those who receive deposits without using the names of banks or shops, in addition to the instruction from the relevant provincial and municipal finance bureaus to follow and implement the case, you should also be informed.

Notices from Both Associations

The Shanghai Banking and Money Trades Association, upon receiving instructions from the Ministry of Finance, has ordered its affiliated banks, silver firms, silver companies, money shops, savings societies, and trust companies to deduct income tax on securities deposit interest from October 1 in accordance with the provisions of the Income Tax Regulations, and to attach Income Tax Instructions and Category D Income Tax Forms. After receiving the order, the two associations immediately mimeographed the original text of the Ministry of Finance and attached the instructions and forms for distribution to all member banks and money shops for compliance. The notice states: "Respectfully, we have received Order No. 29635 from the Ministry of Finance, stating 'The Center Road' etc., and have also issued one hundred copies each of the Collection Instructions and Category D Income Amount Report Forms. With this, we are forwarding them to you accordingly, and attaching two copies each of the Collection Instructions and Report Forms for your inspection and collection. We hope that you will print them yourself according to the format for future use." As for the Shanghai Municipal Government, it has already been ordered to collect income tax on salaries and remuneration of civil servants in accordance with the regulations from yesterday, but at the same time, it has canceled the income donation.

Studying Procedures

The Banking Association has submitted the opinions on income tax collection procedures proposed by the Banking Academy to various member banks for study and solicitation of opinions. Now, various banks have sent their opinions to the association one after another. The association will then compile them and submit them to the Executive Committee for approval before submitting them to the Ministry of Finance for suggestions, hoping to be adopted. The Money Trades Association is scheduled to hold a meeting of member representatives at 2:00 PM today to elect members of the Income Tax Research Committee, and then hold a committee meeting to study various collection procedures. At the same time, the opinions of the Banking Academy will also be studied, and Secretary-General Qin Xieqing will be appointed to consult with Secretary-General Lin Kanghou of the Banking Association on everything as necessary, because both the Banking and Money Trades are financial institutions with the same nature.

Naming Ceremony for Yu Qiaqing Road; Held at the Ningbo Association Yesterday Morning; Racecourse Review of the Chinese Contingent, Myriad of Spectators, Streets Empty; Celebration Ceremony Held at the Association, Grand Ritual 80

In order to commemorate Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 55th anniversary of his journey to Shanghai, all sectors of the city have initiated the renaming of Xizang Road to Yu Qiaqing Road. Yesterday was the day for the implementation of the naming, and there were grand celebrations throughout the day. At 10:00 AM, the Chinese contingent of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps was reviewed at the Racecourse. At noon, a celebration was held at the Ningbo Association. In the evening, the Ningbo Association and the Racecourse performed Peking opera and fireworks. Citizens participated in the celebrations, and the streets were empty. The grand occasion can be described as unprecedented. The details are recorded below:

Ceremony Arrangement

The arrangements for the celebration ceremony were conducted by the preparatory committee, with simplicity and solemnity as the guiding principles. (1) The review of the Chinese contingent of the Volunteer Corps was held at the Racecourse, so the grandstand of the Racecourse on Ma Huo Road was decorated starting the day before yesterday, with flags of all nations hanging along the upper end of the grandstand, fluttering in the wind. A temporary reviewing stand was erected in front of the grandstand, surrounded by our national flags, with several potted plants placed in front of the stand. (2) The venue for the commemorative meeting was set up in the auditorium on the second floor of the Ningbo Association in Shanghai. The main entrance was decorated with a colorful archway made of red and green silk, with the words "Celebrating the Naming Ceremony of Yu Qiaqing Road." In the center of the hall, the national flag of the party and state was hung on the stage, along with silver platters from Jin Tingxun and Du Yuesheng, with inscriptions "Reputation Carried Far and Wide" and "Eternal Preservation of Noble Name," and flower baskets from Zhang Shouyong and others. (3) Along the road, at the southern end at the intersection of Aidoa Road, in the middle around the New World and Daxin Companies on Nanjing Road, and at the northern end at the south end of the Garbage Bridge, colorful silk banners were erected, adorned with the words "Celebrating the Naming Ceremony of Yu Qiaqing Road," attracting the attention of the masses and appearing quite spectacular.

Review Situation

Yesterday's celebration ceremony for the naming of Yu Qiaqing Road and the review of the Chinese contingent of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps began at 10:30 AM at the Racecourse. The presidium included Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Shen Hengfu, and Xu Jikuan, as well as guests Chen Guangfu, Jin Zongcheng, Yuan Ludeng, and Xu Xinliu. On the Chinese contingent side, Chen Shixia, Yuan Hengzhi, Xu Tonghao, and team members from the Chinese and Translators teams, totaling three hundred people, attended. The commander-in-chief was Chen Shixia, with Yu Xiansi, Yang Wenqing, Hao Boyang, Li Yushu, Bao Xianqiang, and Wang Tingkui serving as team leaders. The team first gathered under the clock tower of the Racecourse, and then, led by the Shanghai Municipal Council band, lined up in front of the grandstand, appearing quite orderly and solemn. When Mr. Yu arrived, the audience applauded enthusiastically, and the team members saluted with their guns. Then, accompanied by Xu Tonghao, deputy commander of the Volunteer Corps, and others, Mr. Yu conducted the review, circling around once. Mr. Yu ascended the reviewing stand and gave a speech, saying that the Chinese contingent of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps has a history of thirty years since its establishment, and its service record is excellent. Today, Xizang Road is renamed Yu Qiaqing Road. I am deeply gratified and grateful to all of you for attending this ceremony.

Parade Route

After the review, the team was reorganized for the parade, with the following order: (1) Mounted Patrol, (2) Military Band, (3) Color Guard, (4) Chinese Team, (5) Mr. Yu's Limousine, (6) Translators Team, (7) Representatives of Various Organizations. They proceeded south on Ma Huo Road, east on Aidoa Road to Yu Zhiqing Road, and then north to the front of the Ningbo Association, where Mr. Yu got out of the car and entered the association. Everyone stood at attention to pay their respects. The procession then continued to the Yu Zhiqing Road Bridge and disbanded. The streets were lined with crowds cheering wildly, with no fewer than 300,000 spectators. The Shanghai Municipal Council dispatched a large number of police officers to maintain order along the route. Merchants on both sides set off firecrackers as Mr. Yu's limousine passed by, expressing their admiration. The traffic on the Great, Second, and Third thoroughfares was temporarily suspended. The enthusiasm was unprecedented.

Foreign Guests' Congratulations

Foreign guests who personally attended or sent letters of congratulations on the naming ceremony of Yu Qiaqing Road included: (1) The Diplomatic Corps: German Consul General Krappl, US Vice Consul Kramt, Pol Qiu, Belgian Acting Consul General Tervoort-Flieger, Portuguese Consul General Alvo, Acting Norwegian Consul General Kertel, French Counselor Consul Briot-Veer, Portuguese Consul Aide Montri, Greek Consul General Giannoulis, Brazilian Consul General Brianco, Dutch Consul General Bosewen, Official of the Spanish Consulate-General Fochenafochu, Danish Vice Consul Milqiu, Italian Trade Representative Ligi, Official of the Portuguese Consulate-General Braga, Danish Consul General Ciel; (2) The Shanghai Municipal Council: Chairman Arnold, Director General Jones, Deputy Director General Filipo, Former Chairman Bael, President Feadun, Chairman of the Rickshaw Committee Massey, Director General of the Education Department Shirley, Lawyer of the Legal Department of the Municipal Council Bryan, Deputy Treasurer of the Finance Department Machao, Chief Civil Engineer of the Public Works Department Clark; (3) Foreign Business Guests: Manager of Sassoon & Co. Yesterday the Situation in Hongkou and Zhabei Suddenly Tightened; Japanese Troops Extended Their Posts to the Suzhou Creek; Patrol Posts Along the Border Were Withdrawn Late at Night; Barbed Wire Was Erected at Key Intersections on North Sichuan Road; Two Theories Circulate as to Why the Situation Suddenly Tightened 81

Xinsheng News Agency reports: Since the sniping incident involving Japanese marines in Hongkou on the evening of the 23rd, Japanese Marines, ostensibly to protect overseas Chinese, have been deploying defenses in Hongkou and crossing into Zhabei. The situation had been easing for the past few days. However, yesterday morning, Japanese troops again showed activity, and the situation suddenly seemed to tighten considerably. By late evening, the situation in Hongkou remained the same, while the Zhabei area returned to calm. The actual situation as investigated by a Xinsheng News Agency reporter is as follows:

Japanese Troops Deploy Defenses Reaching the Suzhou Creek

It was found that in the past few days, Japanese troops had only deployed defenses in the concession north of Old Joffre Road. Yesterday, starting from 5:00 AM, the Japanese troops expanded their range, reaching the Suzhou Road and the banks of the Suzhou Creek. They placed sentries along North Sichuan Road and Chapoo Road. Furthermore, they erected barbed wire at the roadsides of key intersections on North Sichuan Road near Old Joffre Road, Haining Road, Peng Road, Wuchang Road, and Tiantong Road, near the Postal Administration, which could block traffic at any time. A light machine gun was also set up at the intersection of Old Joffre Road.

Road Patrols More Frequent Than Before

Japanese troops, centered around the Xingjiaqiao Wan Yongfeng Building on North Sichuan Road, as well as the No. 504 foreign-style house at the intersection of Dixwell Road and Zhimei Road, set up two separate defense posts. Armored vehicles, military trucks, motorcycles, and scattered or organized squads were dispatched to patrol the roads. These patrols, which were originally limited to north of Old Joffre Road, also headed south yesterday, reaching the Suzhou Creek, and the traffic was more frequent than before. At the same time, Japanese troop posts and patrols on Dixwell Road also expanded from the intersection of Tianzheng Road to the Jiaxing Road Bridge yesterday, connecting with the Japanese troops on Wusong Road. Dozens more Japanese troops were stationed at the Japanese Club on Peng Road. Furthermore, nearly every area of the Hongkou region on Haining Road and other roads had Japanese troop posts and patrols. The above is the situation in the concession yesterday before noon. When the reporter went to inspect again around 9:00 PM, the troops stationed at the Japanese Club were gone, with only one post remaining. Other situations such as patrols and barbed wire remained unchanged.

More Posts Set Up in the Zhabei Area

In the Zhabei area, Japanese troops centered their defense posts on the Tanwu Distillery at the end of Huayuan Street and the Japanese Girls' School at the intersection of Ouyang Road and Sida Road. Japanese troops had sentries on the streets of the city on the night of the Hongkou Japanese marine case. The sentries were withdrawn the following night. For the past six days no sentries were sent. Yesterday, starting at 7:00 AM, Japanese troop posts suddenly appeared along Tongbao Road near the intersection of Tongji Road, west to the Yokohama River near the Japanese cemetery, north to the railway crossing on Guangzhong Road, and east to the intersection of Ouyang Road and Shigaoda Road, along Tongji Road, Hengye Road, Jiangwan Road, Xiangde Road, Ouyang Road, Sida Road, and Baoxing Road. On Zhimei Road, Japanese troop posts were sent to Qiaodi No. 1, and all roads were heavily guarded, with almost every hundred or two hundred paces being a double post. All were carrying long guns. At the same time, Japanese troop patrol teams on the above roads were also more frequent than before. However, there were no armored vehicles or barbed wire erected along Tongji Road and Jiangwan Road.

Situation in the City is Peaceful at Night

According to the Xinsheng News Agency reporter's continued investigation last night, the reestablishment of Japanese troop posts in Zhabei was only temporary. It was only from 7:00 AM to 8:30 AM, 11:30 AM to 1:00 PM, and 4:00 PM to 7:00 PM. The purpose was to protect Japanese students. There were many Japanese residences near Jiangwan Road. These three time slots were when Japanese elementary school students were going to school, attending classes, and returning home. Therefore, the situation returned to peace at night. However, troops were stationed all day at the connecting concession and cross-border roads of Ouyang Road, Sida Road, and Zhimei Road, and were not withdrawn until late at night. Yesterday, trucks continued to carry Japanese troops to the Tanwu Distillery, but others were also seen leaving from there. Japanese troops were not seen in the nearby open spaces, probably because they were hidden indoors. Only five people remained guarding the Japanese cemetery.

Two Theories About the Cause of the Tension

There are two theories about why Japanese troops expanded their defenses. One theory is that because the Zhongshan Hidei case was tried and sentenced yesterday, the Japanese troops were putting on a show of force. Another theory is that the barbed wire at the key intersections on North Sichuan Road had already been erected late the night before. This was because a Japanese warship secretly arrived in Shanghai at 1:00 AM yesterday morning, carrying a large number of Japanese troops and military equipment. To avoid drawing attention, the Japanese troops erected the barbed wire. Traffic was once cut off when the Japanese troops landed and transported equipment.

Japanese Embassy and Consulate Offer No Comment

Japanese diplomats have not commented on the actions of Japanese troops. The reporter went to the Japanese embassy to inquire yesterday. The representative of its information department replied to the reporter with the usual response, saying that they do not know the Marine Corps' actions unless they voluntarily publish them. Furthermore, the newly appointed Third Secretary of the Japanese Embassy stated that he had gone to Beijing a few days ago to meet with Japanese Ambassador Kawagoe, report his arrival in Shanghai, and convey instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. He returned to Shanghai yesterday morning with another secretary of the Japanese Embassy who had previously gone to Beijing.

Yang Hucheng's Bad Tooth Has Been Removed 82

No Significant Progress in Heart Condition

Yang Hucheng, the Pacification Commissioner of Shaanxi, came to Shanghai last month to seek treatment for a tooth ailment at the Shanghai Sanitarium and Hospital. He then moved to the Hongqiao Sanitarium and Hospital to treat his heart condition. It is now learned that Mr. Yang's bad tooth has been extracted and he is currently having a denture fitted. However, there has been no significant progress in his heart condition. Mr. Yang originally planned to go to Guangdong to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, but later learned that Chairman Chiang was about to leave Guangdong, so he stopped his trip south. Then, when Chairman Chiang arrived in Jiangxi from Guangdong, Mr. Yang telegraphed to inquire about the location and time for a meeting. As soon as he receives a reply, he will proceed to meet with him according to instructions.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Hosted the National Goods Exhibition, Which Opened Yesterday; Wang Xiaolai Cut the Ribbon and Xu Xiaochu Raised the Flag; Dozens of Representatives from Party and Government Circles Attended 83

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, in commemoration of the 15th anniversary of the Exhibition Hall, held a National Goods Exhibition at Jing'an Temple Road. It opened at 2:00 PM yesterday. Many guests from all walks of life attended. The details are recorded as follows:

Guests Attending

The National Goods Exhibition is scheduled to last for three weeks. If needed, the exhibition period can be extended. At the same time, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce's Exhibition Hall will also expand its scope and display samples of national goods for people to visit. The guests of honor attending the opening ceremony yesterday included President Wang Xiaolai, Vice President Xu Xiaochu, Mao Yun from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Song Zhongqing from the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, Sun Daosheng from the Citizens' National Goods Promotion Association, Xu Genghua from the National Goods Maintenance Association, Wang Xingyao from the China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperation Association, and committee members and representatives from various manufacturers, including Hu Xiyuan, Cai Shengbai, Pan Yangyao, Zhang Huikang, Yuan Ludeng, Mao Heyuan, Fang Jiaobo, Fang Jiange, Luo Qinghua, and dozens of others.

Exhibition Venue Arrangement

The exhibition venue had two entrances, both with brightly colored archways that were very eye-catching. Inside, each manufacturer arranged and displayed their products according to their respective locations. There were many styles and a wide variety of products, indicating the rapid progress of national goods. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Boy Scouts maintained order inside and outside the venue, and staff from the association were on-site to take care of matters. At the opening ceremony, the Municipal Police Bureau band played music, and Zhu Boyuan served as the master of ceremonies. President Wang Xiaolai cut the ribbon to the music, and then Vice President Xu Xiaochu raised the flag of the National Goods Exhibition. Then, they led the guests to visit various parts of the venue and distributed special issues of the conference. Finally, tea and refreshments were served until 3:00 PM.

Chairman's Report

Then, Chairman Wang Xiaolai reported: "Distinguished guests, it is our great honor that you have graced the opening of the National Goods Exhibition today. The main reason for holding this exhibition is to commemorate the 15th anniversary of the establishment of the Goods Exhibition Hall. It has achieved many accomplishments in the past, so we are launching this exhibition as a commemoration. The Goods Exhibition Hall is affiliated with the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and is dedicated to promoting national goods. For example, it has hosted national goods exhibitions, added national goods bazaars, assisted overseas Chinese and foreigners in purchasing national goods, and introduced the buying and selling of national goods. It has a considerable history in the national goods industry. Today, we will continue to strive to uphold our original intentions. However, because preparations were rushed, many things may be lacking. We sincerely hope that patriotic men and women will provide guidance."

President's Speech

Next, Vice President Xu Xiaochu gave a speech: "Our association believes that in this era of commercial warfare, to promote the development of domestic goods, we must create more opportunities for producers and consumers to interact. National goods exhibitions are the best way to achieve this because they allow manufacturers to understand how to improve, and the public can purchase without being fooled by foreign imitations. In recent years, due to changes in the mindset of the Chinese people and the efforts of promotion, the trade deficit has been decreasing. This is a good sign of strengthening the country. I hope that everyone will continue to uphold their patriotic intentions, promote and advocate, so that the national goods industry can flourish." Hu Xiyuan, Pan Yangyao, Wang Xingyao, and others then gave speeches. At the same time, for the sake of widespread publicity, Zhou Bangjun will be broadcasting on the Sino-Western Radio Station and Xu Xiaochu will be broadcasting on the Mainland Radio Station every day.

General Assembly Declaration

Tracing back to our Chinese nation, since the opening of the seas in the late Qing Dynasty, the great powers have relied on their unequal treaties as a talisman to carry out economic aggression against us, dumping their surplus products. Like mercury pouring to the ground, they have flooded in and seized markets everywhere. The Chinese people have been fickle, worshiping foreign goods, resulting in an outflow of money and endless troubles. Self-sufficient industries and businesses have been destroyed, and the unemployed population has increased, causing social and economic decline. However, merchants are still bound by old laws, stuck in their ways. Craftsmen are still sticking to old rules, not thinking about improvements. Others use machinery while we are only manual. How can we stem the tide of the trade deficit? Since the May Fourth Movement, the Chinese people have suffered under the threat of imperialism, deeply feeling the pain of economic aggression. They know that to save the country and resist insults, invigorating national goods is essential. As a result, factories have been gradually established everywhere, and the output of national goods has been increasing day by day. However, there is a lack of communication and cooperation, resulting in very little effect. Patriotic people are deeply troubled by this, and are collecting samples of national goods, setting up exhibition halls, leading to observation and encouraging their use, so as to increase identification capabilities and avoid confusion with imitations. This is the best method. Unfortunately, it is often motivated by temporary indignation. After things have passed, they give up. They never finish what they start, leaving foreigners with the criticism of a "five-minute fever." There has never been anyone who has persevered, redoubling their efforts, like our Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce's Goods Exhibition Hall, which has been established since 1921, holding on with perseverance and determination, not being discouraged by adverse environments, nor stopping halfway due to bleak prospects. Isn't this how national goods should be promoted? One cannot expect to achieve everything in one fell swoop. However, their spirit of perseverance and hard work can serve as a model for our manufacturers. Therefore, on the occasion of this 15th anniversary, we must commemorate it. Thinking about today's environment, although the national goods industry has been promoted by people all over the country, it has declined as before, and social and economic panic has deepened. Could it be that the Chinese people are still stuck in the misconception that domestic goods must be crude and foreign goods must be superior, and are rejecting domestic goods? Or are there those who have lost their minds and are replacing domestic goods with foreign goods, changing their appearance? These two are obstacles to the future of domestic goods, and those who love and use domestic goods should pay attention, and our manufacturers should strive to improve day and night. Therefore, in addition to the celebration, we are holding an expanded national goods exhibition, collecting and displaying new and old products from various factories to seek advice from the Chinese people. We hope that those who love and use national goods and want to recognize national goods will carefully distinguish them to avoid being deceived. Those who believe that national goods must be crude will also know that today's national goods are no longer what they used to be. We also hope that everyone will evaluate which ones are superior, which ones are inferior, which ones are suitable for society, and which ones are out of date, and provide guidance as much as possible, so as to improve them. We must be of one mind, help each other, cooperate, and persevere to make the national goods industry flourish day by day, and comfort the grand plan of the founders of the Exhibition Hall. This is what the manufacturers are praying for.

The Japanese Marine Case Was Announced Today; Lawyers on Both Sides Hold Their Own Reasons; Debate Concluded Yesterday 85

The case of Yang Wendao, Ye Haisheng (nicknamed Little Guangdong), Zhou Sherong, etc., all from Guangdong, who are accused of killing Japanese marine Zhongshan Hideio, was previously announced to be concluded by the First Special District Court. However, because witnesses still needed to be questioned, the announcement was revoked and the investigation was continued. The fingerprints of Yang Wendao and Yang Jianzhong and the books hiding the handgun found in Yang's house were sent to the Zhenru Forensic Medicine Institute for identification. On the 24th of last month, the institute sent a detailed report of the identification results to the court. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Presiding Judge Qian Hongye and Assessors Feng Shide and Xiao Xiefei

convened a collegiate bench for deliberation. Prosecutor Tang also attended the court to perform his duties. The security inside and outside the courtroom remained strict, but only ordinary personnel from the Japanese side attended the hearing, with no armed soldiers. After the judges took their seats, they first ordered Clerk Ding Zhongnan to read the identification report from the Forensic Medicine Institute. Then, Presiding Judge Qian questioned Yang Wendao about the origin of the books. Yang still denied that he owned the books. The court then announced that the evidence had been fully investigated and ordered the debate to begin. The reasons that had been stated previously should not be repeated. First, the lawyer for the police, Ru Baoyi, spoke, stating that after the

re-investigation of the evidence, the testimonies of witnesses who appeared in court, such as Pan Qiaoying and Yang Jianzhong, were sufficient to supplement the points that were still unclear and doubtful before. Therefore, after the witnesses testified, he felt that the facts investigated previously were very clear, and Yang Wendao claimed that the book containing the gun found in his house was planted by Yang Jianzhong. Yang Jianzhong also testified in court that he had no intention of planting the evidence, and the Forensic Medicine Institute had verified that there were no Jianzhong fingerprints on the book, so Wendao bears full responsibility for this book. In addition, there were no new developments regarding the two defendants, Ye and Zhou, and the testimonies from other aspects were sufficient to prove that they were consistent with Ye's

confession, and that the confession was credible. In short, the case has reached a point where there is no doubt, and he requested that the defendants be sentenced to death. Then, lawyers Tang Huaiqun and Guo Qiming defended Yang Wendao and Zhou Sherong, mainly focusing on the point that the book containing the gun was found in Yang's house. Since the Forensic Medicine Institute had verified that there were no fingerprints of Yang Jianzhong in the book, Yang Wendao's claim that it was planted by Jianzhong was not credible, but the institute also verified that there were no fingerprints of Yang Wendao left in the book, so it could be determined that the book was not the original book found in Yang's house. Yang

was not involved with the book. Zhou was falsely implicated by Ye. They should both be acquitted. Finally, lawyers Zhang Zhirang, Wang Shizong, Fan Gang, and others defended Ye Haisheng. They all stated that many of the testimonies of the witnesses who were called this time were in favor of the defendant, especially Pan Qiaoying's statement that she saw the murderer walking shoulder to shoulder with the victim before the shooting was consistent with the forensic examination of the victim's injuries, which was enough to

break Ye's confession that he fired the shot. Finally, Prosecutor Tang rose to argue, stating that the case had been heard many times, and he requested that a judgment be made according to the law. Presiding Judge Qian then announced the conclusion of the debate and set the judgment for the afternoon of the second day (today). He also ordered that the defendants be returned to custody.

Sino-Japanese International Wireless Telephone Opens Service to Hakodate and Otaru 86

Since the opening of the Sino-Japanese international wireless telephone service in February, Yokohama, Osaka, Tokyo, Nagoya, Kyoto, and other places have successively opened calls with Shanghai. Hakodate and Otaru in Hokkaido have completed preparations and opened calls with this city at noon yesterday. Beforehand, the International Telecommunications Bureau and the Japanese Telecommunications Bureau in Hakodate and Otaru had trial calls, and the sound was exceptionally clear. The call fee is the same as other areas: 15 yuan for each three-minute call, and 5 yuan is added for each additional minute.

Blood Soul Assassination Corps Members Confess to Bombing; Second Special Court Interrogates All Defendants in Detail Yesterday; Wang Dongcai Confesses that the Headquarters is in the Samsung Factory 87

Liu Hantao, Chuan Chaofu, Yin Jiafu, Wang Dongcai, Guan Yaoting, and other five members of the Blood Soul Assassination Corps were arrested for throwing bombs at shops in the International Settlement. They were sentenced to imprisonment by the First Special Court. The French Concession police, after finding that Liu and others had also committed similar crimes in the French Concession, requested the Second Special Court to transfer Liu and others to the case for investigation and detention. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. It is now learned that the case was found by the French Police Department to be that the defendants threw bombs at Xie Da Xiang Foreign Goods Store on Xiaodongmen Street, Yuanhe Sugar Store at 130 Minquan Road, Bei Runsheng's house on Beile Road, Deshengxiang Foreign Goods Store on Fada Road, and Rixinsheng Foreign Goods Store on the afternoon of November 18, 1935. The lawyer from the Medical Affairs Office filed a public lawsuit based on Article 151, Article 154, and Article 181 of the Criminal Law for disrupting order and endangering public safety. Yesterday morning, Assessor Chen Shuoying from the Second Special Court continued the trial in Criminal Court No. 1. According to Liu Hantao's confession, he joined the Assassination Corps in 1933. Wang Tiemin gave him a bomb in Yuqing Lane on Nanjing Road and ordered him to throw it at Xie Da Xiang in Xiaodongmen. He gave a warning at the counter door. Chuan Chaofu confessed that he joined the Assassination Corps because he knew Wang Dongcai and was introduced by him. He had never thrown a bomb, but he knew that they had bombed twice. The agency was in Zhang Zilian's house. On July 28 of this year, he went to Zhang's house to ask for a job. Zhang sent Zhang Zongfu to see him and told him to go again on August 3. When he went there, he was arrested. Yin Jiafu confessed that he joined the group in the first half of 1933. They went to see the location and asked him to throw the bomb. The first time was a sugar shop in the 16th pier, the second time was Deshengxiang Foreign Goods Store on Fada Road, and the third time was Rixinsheng Foreign Goods Store. He was arrested and sentenced to four months in prison with a two-year reprieve. The bomb was made of sulfur and would not hurt people. Wang Dongcai confessed that he joined the group in the second half of 1932. The agency was in the distribution office of the Samsung Cotton Weaving Factory. He went with Yin to throw bombs twice, and he went to Bei Runsheng's house alone once. Guan Yaoting confessed that he threw a bomb at Yufeng Foreign Goods Store in Dongxinqiao once. Then, Zhang Hengzhong, a staff member of Yufeng Store, testified that he found a bomb exploding at the window at 6:00 PM one day in May 1933, shattering the glass. He did not know them. In addition, Wang Yanong, the representative of Bei Runsheng, appeared in court. The court ordered Bei himself to appear in court for questioning next time. Then, the lawyer from the Police Department stated that in addition to prosecuting Chuan Chaofu under Article 154 of the Criminal Law, the remaining defendants were prosecuted under Article 151 and Article 187 of the Criminal Law. The court verified the words and adjourned the hearing to the morning of the 14th and ordered the defendants to be returned to custody.

Courtroom Packed; Continued Hearing of the Box Murder Case; Mao A'gen and Jiang Yuan'tan Completely Retract Confessions; Resolutely Deny Killing Caiying 90

Only Lin Gendi Speaks Unequivocally

Since the headless box murder case occurred, although the Hongkou Police Department's Chinese detectives Huang Fusen, Liu Zhaonian, etc., captured three female suspects, Lin Gendi, Mao A'gen, and Jiang Qian'yuan Tan, the testimonies of Mao and Jiang were inconsistent, sometimes admitting and sometimes denying, making the case confusing and difficult to understand. Zhong Qing, the judge of the First Special District Court presiding over the case, personally visited the scene of the incident at 3 Cunfu Lane, Baibao Road, for an on-site investigation in order to understand the truth. However, the outcome did not yield many clues. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM was the scheduled date for the continued hearing of the case. The general public, driven by curiosity, flocked to the court to listen, so the large second courtroom was

packed to the rafters, and many were turned away. The defendant Mao A'gen hired lawyer Fan Gang, and Jiang Qian'yuan Tan hired lawyer Shen Xiaoxiang, to defend them in court. First, Judge Zhong questioned the defendant Lin Gendi. According to Lin, her previous testimony about Mao and Jiang killing Caiying was entirely true. As for disposing of the body, it was on the third day after the killing. Counting the day of the killing, it should be the fourth day, so

the day of the crime was definitely August 8th. However, she did not hold Caiying's mouth at the time, and Caiying did not cry for help. She only saw her feet twitching slightly. After Chang Jiang used an ax to injure Caiying's head, she ran away, and so on. According to Mao A'gen Hong, on August 8th, from 3 PM onwards, he drove the second-in-command of the fire brigade's car to the Gonghexiang Wharf to send passengers onto ships. At around 4 PM, he drove the car again to take the chief to the Hongkou Fire Brigade to play ball. At 8 PM, he went to the Yangshupu Weituoma Road Water Plant at the request of a friend. At that time, the chief ordered the car to be parked at the Yangshupu Police Department. It was not until midnight that he drove the car again to pick up the chief and take him home, so regarding

the killing of Caiying, not only was he completely unaware, but he also had no time to participate. Police Department lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that the Police Department had already obtained Mao A'gen Jiang Yuanying's work reports from August 7th onwards. However, regarding the work on August 8th, there was a separate form, which recorded roughly the same as what Mao had stated, but in the afternoon, the car was not driven out. After the last adjournment, the Police Department had sent Mao to the Engineering Bureau Hospital, and Lin Gendi was sent to the Guangren Hospital. Both were examined and found to have gonorrhea, but whether they had syphilis could

not be determined. Regarding the last time, lawyer Fan Gang raised the newspaper report that the Engineering Bureau doctor had stated that the body was killed no more than 24 hours before it was discovered. However, the Police Department had also investigated, and according to the Engineering Bureau Hospital's report, the maximum was 24 hours because modern medicine really cannot clarify this point. Moreover, Mao had admitted everything the last time the court went to the Police Department to question him, so he did not know why he suddenly retracted his confession today, and so on. The court immediately questioned Mao based on this. According to him, the reason for his previous admission was because he could not bear the suffering and made a false confession. In reality, that was not the case. He was also asked

where the deceased's clothes were now. He answered that he really did not know. Jiang Yuanying was also questioned and completely denied it. "In good conscience, I have never seen Caiying. The reason I confessed last time was because I could not bear the torture," and so on. At this time, the defendant's lawyer, Fan Gang, immediately stated that this case concerns human life and is of great importance. Therefore, whether Caiying existed, whether she had family members, and whether she lived at No. 2 Cunfu Lane, where she lived before, and her usual interactions with Lin Gendi, etc., all need to be thoroughly investigated. Lawyer Shen Xiaoxiang also requested that the Public Security Bureau investigate the household registration to clarify whether Caiying lived there. Then, Judge Zhong announced,

"During the autopsy, the forensic doctor determined that the deceased was still alive when she was killed and was not stabbed after death," and so on. When questioned about Lin Gendi's testimony, he said that he had only known the reporter for a week, and they were both female receptionists at the Daxin Company amusement park for only three days. Her accent seemed to be from Changzhou. Mao A'gen also testified that on August 11th, he drove the car until 4:50 PM before returning to the fire brigade. At that time, he bathed, washed clothes, and after dinner, he played mahjong with fire brigade members No. 100 and No. 125, etc., for a thousand rounds. How could he have any free time to

go to dispose of the body? It was all Lin Gendi's false accusation. Lin immediately argued with Mao upon hearing this, saying that it was not a false accusation. The court then asked Mao whether he had gone to the Zhonghua Hotel with Lin Gendi on August 9th to open a room. Mao denied it. Then, the tea boy from the Zhonghua Hotel testified that around 11 PM on the 9th, someone did come to open a room. Then, they heard a woman's voice in the room, but they did not know whether it was Lin Gendi. The court then asked Lin Gendi, "When you disposed of the body, was it already smelly?" He answered

that it did not smell yet. Then, Chinese detective Huang Fusen testified that between 2:55 PM and 3:30 PM on September 21st, he took Lin Gendi to the Daxin Amusement Park to meet a Zhang surname inspector, who took out all the photos of the female tea servers and asked Lin to identify them. However, Lin said that there was no photo of Caiying in the photos. At that time, according to Inspector Zhang, Caiying had only worked for three days and was not an official female tea server, so there was no photo. He also stated that when Lin Gendi

was a female tea server at the company, she was fired for stealing someone else's wallet. Later, the two defendants, Mao and Jiang, pleaded with the small foreman Xiao Debao, and she was reinstated. Now, the Zhang surname has resigned. If the court believes it is necessary to summon him, he can be found again. Judge Zhong, considering that this case is of great importance and has many doubtful points, should be thoroughly investigated. Therefore, he ruled that the case be adjourned to the afternoon of the 15th of this month for further hearing, and summoned the person in charge of managing the female tea servers at the Daxin Company and the old woman who lived at No. [blank] Cunfu Lane to appear in court as witnesses.

Buddha Image Found in Giant Clam; Clasped Hands in Lotus Position; Features Perfectly Depicted 96

Xiang Songshan, a villager from Xicun Village, Yangjing Township, Baoshan County, recently found a large clam on the beach, weighing four or five jin, extremely large, and with a hard shell. Its ears, eyes, mouth, and nose were perfectly depicted. Xiang was overjoyed to obtain this treasure and cherished it, unwilling to show it to others easily, intending to sell it for a good price.

Sun Fuxi Congratulates the Three Heroines on Their Success 99

Sun Fuxi, the president of the Yifeng Society, wrote an article entitled "Congratulating the Three Heroines' Painting Exhibition on Its Success in Promoting Abroad." The following is an excerpt of the main points: Chinese flowers have made brilliant contributions in literature and painting. Not only has the depiction of flowers established rich and excellent characteristics in Chinese art and literature, but it has also opened up a vast and beautiful area for world art and literature. The Western art world greatly admires the superb and profound depiction of Chinese flowers, feeling inferior. This is because Chinese literature and painting can use extremely subtle observation and extremely flexible rendering, not only capturing the likeness of the form but also expressing the spirit vividly and with vitality. Furthermore, through symbolic methods, everything can be imbued with life, and everything can represent human emotions. Thus, there is poetry in painting, and painting in poetry. Beautiful women and fragrant herbs can all convey the greatest emotions of joy, anger, love, and hate. Those who recently ridiculed romantic poetry as indulging in pleasure and neglecting ambition do not understand the true meaning of flowers and the moon in Chinese art and literature but merely criticize their misuse. The Xiong sisters are three conjoined flowers of China. Their depiction of flowers deeply captures the essence of the Ouxiang school. This time, they have been sent by the Ministry to various countries in the West to hold exhibitions of their works, which can greatly promote the brilliance of Chinese art. With this in mind, I wish them success in advance.

Owners of Private Handcarts; Order Your Rickshaw Pullers to Obtain Licenses Quickly 103

The licenses for rickshaw pullers of private handcarts in the Public Concession expired on September 30. From the 1st of this month, new licenses should be renewed. This matter has already been announced by the Engineering Bureau's Donation Department. Owners of private handcarts, if their rickshaw pullers have not yet gone to obtain licenses, or if they are unclear about the licensing methods, should immediately provide guidance. All license numbers from No. 1 to No. 5,000 should apply for renewal from October 1st to October 20th. Those with license numbers from No. 5,001 to No. 8,000 should apply for renewal from October 21st to November 4th. Those with license numbers above 8,000 should apply for renewal from November 5th to November 16th. All rickshaw pullers of private handcarts should pay attention to carrying their existing license and arm badge during the specified dates to apply for renewal at the Engineering Bureau rickshaw puller licensing office on Shunde Road, Xinzha. The sooner the better. From November 16th of this year, rickshaw pullers of private handcarts who do not have a new license and wear an arm badge in a conspicuous place on their left arm will not be allowed to pull a rickshaw. Furthermore, the license renewal fee is 50 cents in national currency within the specified period, and one yuan in national currency after the deadline.

A grand tea party was held at 5 p.m. to thank all sectors and also announce the closing. Members from other cities departed from Shanghai starting last night. The detailed report is as follows:

Yesterday's Visits

All members, including Ma Yinchu, Li Zhao Huan, Li Quan Shi, and over one hundred and ten others, gathered at the Eight Immortals Bridge at 8:30 yesterday morning. They divided into east and west groups and departed in chartered buses. (1) East Group: Visited the Commercial Press Printing House, Beikaier Road; Shanghai Electric Power Company, Yangshupu Road, in the morning; and Jiangnan University, Yangshupu Road, for lunch (at Jiangnan University) at noon. In the afternoon, they visited Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, Jungong Road; the Clearing House, Hong Kong Road; Wing On Textile Factory No. 1, Yangshupu Lan Road; and the Wusong seaside. At 5 p.m., there was a tea party at the International Hotel, Jing'an Temple Road, Parker Road. (2) West Group: Visited the Zhonghua Book Company Printing House, Macau Road; Shanghai Telephone Company, Maite Hesitesi Road; the Central Mint, at the end of Gordon Road, in the morning; and Jiaotong University, Haig Road, for lunch (at Jiaotong University) at noon. In the afternoon, they visited the Institute of Physics and Textiles, Academia Sinica, Bailinan Road; Longhua Cement Factory, Longhua; and Guanshengyuan Farm, Caohejing.

Grand Tea Party

The society held a grand tea party at 5 p.m. yesterday afternoon on the second floor of the International Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road to thank all sectors and also announce the closing. Attendees included members Li Zhaoshuai, Ma Yinchu, Mu Ouchu, Chuan Rulin, Qian Xinzhi, He Dekui, Wang Zhixin, Cheng Shaode, Zhu Binyuan, Bu Kai, Cai Zhengya, Lin Kanghou, Li Yunliang, Chen Changheng, Huang Renzhi, and guests Wang Xiaoji, Du Yuesheng, Zai Boqi, Hu Xiyuan, Xu Peihuang, Cai Jingjun, Liu Haisu, Xi Yushu, Xiang Kangyuan, Kui Yanfang, Jin Runxiang, He Bingsong, Zheng Zhao, Chen Jicheng, Zhu Shaoping, and over three hundred others. Ma Yinchu gave the closing speech (recorded separately). Hu Qingrong, Xi Yushu, Chuan Rulin, Zhu Shaoping, Bu Kai, and others then spoke successively, acknowledging the great contribution of this annual meeting of the society to the important issues facing Chinese society and the economy today. National economic issues have been generally recognized by the public as important problems for society and the nation. The society's members, based on their academic and professional knowledge, can contribute to society and the nation, which is of great benefit. It is hoped that they will continue to work hard for the country and society in this spirit. The event ended happily at 6:30 p.m.

Closing Speech

Chairman Ma Yinchu delivered a closing speech, summarized as follows: (1) The 13th Annual Meeting of our society was held in Shanghai. We are very grateful for the sincere hospitality of various cultural groups and industrial and commercial groups in Shanghai. (2) The number of our society's members has increased year by year. Branches have been established in Hunan, Guangdong, Tianjin, Hangzhou, Nanjing, and Shanghai. Members are either specialized in academics or have extensive experience. The goal is to establish a very close connection between academic thought and the actual environment. (3) The country has faced many difficulties in recent years. Facing the oppression of strong neighbors, a glimmer of hope remains. Saving the nation depends entirely on the cooperation of the academic and business communities. (4) In recent years, domestic capital has been depleted, rural areas have gone bankrupt, and the purchasing power of the majority of the people in the country is weak, affecting industry and commerce. To seek economic revival, we must attach equal importance to agriculture and industry. Our country's biggest problem lies in one-sided or partial development. The difference between rural areas and cities (such as Shanghai) is almost a hundred years. This is not enough to plan for the overall economy in peacetime, and it is not easy to resist foreign aggression in wartime. We must develop national transportation, connecting east, west, north, and south, develop inland resources, improve the lives of farmers, and ensure that agriculture, industry, commerce, and mining develop equally and consistently, without any imbalance. Only then can we talk about prosperity and equality. If all the country's floating capital is concentrated in Shanghai, used solely for speculation in peacetime, and then flees overseas in wartime, both the national economy and the people's livelihood will suffer. We must be wary of this. I hope the financial giants in Shanghai will pay attention to this. (5) Finally, I hope that members of our society will work even harder for the society's affairs than before. We ask that anyone who studies economics, as well as those who have achieved success in the business community, be introduced at any time to achieve the purpose of collective wisdom. (6) Under today's circumstances, academic thought should not be too far removed from the environment, but must stand on the front line as the standard for all actions of the society. For example, our country only has a financial market, not a capital market. Even this financial market is very disorganized. Therefore, members of our society who occupy important positions in the financial community, such as Mr. Xu Jilun, Jin Luqin, Wang Zhixin, Zhang Naiqi, and Yang Yinpu, have spared no effort in promoting bill discounting and acceptance, which has now become a reality. This alone proves that thought is the mother of fact, but this kind of thought should adapt to the needs of society and not be too far removed from the environment. Now some people are advocating a capital market, opening stock trading in the stock exchange, and selling prices of company bonds, so that social floating capital can move from the road of speculation to investment, giving the agricultural, industrial, and mining industries the opportunity to use domestic capital. Isn't this a major undertaking at present? I hope that members of our society will continue to work hard to achieve success. (7) Recently, I read in the newspapers that Rogers, who returned to China with Sir Ross last time, is now back in China as a financial advisor to our country. It is said that it is very difficult for China to use foreign capital because there are many obstacles. I believe that to seek economic recovery, we must use foreign capital. Since it is so difficult to use foreign capital, we can only use domestic capital to make up for the deficiency. Therefore, domestic capital must not be squandered on foreigners again. Recently, I heard that people in Shanghai with capital are engaged in speculative trading of foreign stocks and securities. According to a famous lawyer in Shanghai, this speculation often leads to lawsuits, and Chinese people always lose, causing countless bankruptcies. Millions of good money are unconditionally squandered in the hands of foreigners, which is truly inexcusable. I hope the financial authorities will ban it as soon as possible. Even if they cannot ban it, they should at least regulate it. Brokers must register, and transactions must pay evidence money, so that speculation will have a certain limit. I hope that members of this society and various cultural groups will work together to promote this, create an atmosphere first, and then implement regulation. (8) From the perspective of today's national situation, free competition and free trade are not suitable for China, because some countries are using improper methods to seize our business. Since the methods are improper, competition is not free. We should also resist it with unfree methods. The so-called unfree method is regulation. Regulation means using the power of the group to achieve the purpose of self-salvation. To seek China's freedom, we must sacrifice individual freedom. If 400 million compatriots sing freedom, they will be like a pile of loose sand, how can they resist foreign aggression? If the whole country can proceed in unison, a small enemy country is not to be feared. Now it is a matter of life and death. I hope that everyone present has a very clear understanding of today's economic issues.

Central Mint: New Coins Minted in September 109

Announcement No. 38 of the Auditing Committee of the Central Mint states: This is an announcement regarding the fact that in September of the 25th year [1936], the Central Mint minted Class B thousand-yuan bars (880 fineness) from number 58607 to number 58946, totaling 340 bars. The committee appointed chemical examiner Ge Laide to supervise the stamping according to regulations and register the fineness and weight of each bar in a list. In the same month, the factory produced subsidiary coins, including 8.9 million 20-cent nickel coins, 9.3 million 10-cent nickel coins, and 30.16 million 1-cent copper coins. All three types of subsidiary coins were supervised and sealed by personnel sent by the committee. In addition to being allowed to leave the factory separately, a detailed table is attached for general knowledge. This announcement is made by Chairman Kong Xiangxi on October 1st.

Japanese Warship "Hayayuki" Sailed from Shanghai Yesterday 110

Six Remaining Ships Docked in Shanghai

According to Xin Sheng She, the Japanese destroyer "Hayayuki," which arrived in Shanghai on the 27th of last month, suddenly left the port at 2:25 p.m. yesterday, destination unknown. According to a Xin Sheng She reporter's investigation yesterday, there were still six Japanese warships docked in Shanghai as of last night. They include the cruiser "Izumo" (i.e., the flagship of the Japanese Third Fleet, docked at the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha wharf on Huangpu Road) and the destroyers "Fumizuki" (docked at the Mitsui head wharf in Pudong), "Minazuki," "Nagatsuki," "Shiokaze," and "Shimokaze" (all docked at the East Mitsui wharf).

Foreign Warships Arrive in Shanghai to Protect Overseas Chinese; Two American Warships Arrived Yesterday 111

Fleet Commander Murphy Arrives

According to Xin Sheng She, foreign warships at other ports are arriving in Shanghai one after another to prevent the deterioration of the situation in Shanghai and to protect overseas Chinese. Rear Admiral Murphy, commander of the U.S. Asiatic Fleet, arrived in Shanghai on the flagship USS Augusta from Qinhuangdao at 9:55 a.m. yesterday, anchored at the 14th and 15th buoys. The small U.S. warship USS Asheville, which came from Qingdao, also entered the port at 11:25 a.m. yesterday and anchored at the 2nd and 3rd buoys in the upper reaches of the Huangpu River. The U.S. gunboat USS Monocacy, which was originally docked in Shanghai, left the port at 7:50 a.m. yesterday and sailed to Beijing to be stationed. According to the U.S. Naval Transportation Office, other ships of the U.S. Asiatic Fleet, except for one or two ships undergoing repairs in Manila, the large ship USS Black Hawk and eleven destroyers, as well as the gunboat USS Canopus and many auxiliary ships, will arrive in Shanghai successively from the 16th of this month. According to a survey conducted by reporters at customs yesterday, in addition to the Japanese warships (see separate item), the foreign ships currently docked in Shanghai include the U.S. small warship USS Asheville, the British gunboat HMS Bee, the British destroyer HMS Duncan, the Italian gunboat Ermanno Carlotto, the French gunboat Francis Garnier, the U.S. transport ship USS Gold Star, the U.S. gunboat USS Guam, the Italian gunboat Lepanto, the British gunboat HMS Mantis, the U.S. small warship USS Tulsa, and the two U.S. warships that just arrived in Shanghai yesterday, for a total of twelve ships.

Lawyer Ma Junshuo Officially Begins Practice Today 113

Dr. Ma Junshuo, a famous lawyer, was specially appointed by the Judicial Yuan of the National Government last year to visit Europe and the United States to investigate the judicial systems of various countries. He visited more than ten countries, including England, the United States, Germany, France, Italy, Japan, and Switzerland. Everywhere he went, he was personally received by administrative and judicial leaders and justices and prosecutors of the Supreme Court of each country, and he was warmly welcomed. At the same time, Lawyer Ma also promoted the progress of China's judiciary and the improvement of laws in various countries, allowing people around the world to understand the current state of China's administration and judiciary. After Vice President Tan, Lawyer Ma is truly the first person to have earned a reputation in Europe and the United States for studying legal systems around the world. After returning to China, Mr. Ma reported his findings to the government, which was highly praised by the authorities. He also compiled his findings into a book for the reference of the Chinese people. This work is currently being printed and will be published soon. Currently, due to the large number of old and new cases, clients have been constantly asking him to perform his duties. In order to implement his purpose of protecting people's rights, Mr. Ma has decided to officially start his practice today. The office is located at Room 608, 6th Floor, Continental Commercial Building, telephone numbers 94567 and 92732. Mr. Ma gained a lot of experience in the lawyer systems of various countries during this trip, and he will be able to further promote the system of lawyer in our country in the future.

Total amount of exchange coupon reserve: 25,686,815 yuan, including: 15,681,564.83 yuan in cash reserve and 10,005,2469.17 yuan in guarantee reserve. The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated: The Shandong area and the lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy and cool, with strong northerly winds. The Yellow River basin and the upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy and clear, with uncertain wind directions. The center of the hurricane was within 30 miles of 25.30 degrees north latitude and 127.30 degrees east longitude at 2 p.m., with strong winds. Our Country's Olympic Delegation Arrives in Shanghai Tomorrow Afternoon; Li Huitang, Who Passed Through Hong Kong Yesterday Morning, Has Landed; Wang Zhengting Talks About Popularizing Sports as Soon as Possible 119

Yesterday morning, the National Sports Advancement Association received a telegram from Wang Zhengting, the leader of the Olympic delegation, from Hong Kong, stating, "The entire delegation is on the Italian mail ship Conte Rosso and has now safely arrived in Hong Kong. It will arrive in Shanghai the day after tomorrow (3rd) afternoon."

Hong Kong, 1st: Our Olympic delegation of more than one hundred people, led by Wang Zhengting, returned home from Europe on the Italian ship Conte Rosso. They arrived in Hong Kong at 7 a.m. on the 1st, and many people came to the port to welcome them. Except for 24 people, including Li Huitang and Yang Xiuqiong, who landed in Hong Kong, the rest returned to Shanghai on the original ship at noon.

Hong Kong, 1st: Wang Zhengting led the Olympic delegation through Hong Kong on the 1st on their way home and gave a speech on the ship, saying that China's sports are backward. To compete with the world's strong teams, we must strengthen our forces. To catch up, we must first popularize sports. Our country's participation in the Olympics is to attract the attention of people across the country so that they can encourage each other to strive for progress in the future. This move by our government is the first step in promoting national sports. We were warmly welcomed during this trip. The martial arts team gave many performances and were well received. The football team went to various European countries to compete. The performance against England was better than expected. The next Olympics will be held in Japan, and our country hopes to send more athletes to organize a strong team to participate.

(Hong Kong, 1st) The Olympic athletes, led by Wang Zhengting, arrived in Hong Kong at 6 a.m. on the 1st. Various sports associations sent representatives to welcome the team members. As there was not much time to stay in Hong Kong, they did not attend the welcome meeting of the Sports Association. Except for the Hong Kong and Guangdong team members, the rest returned to Shanghai on the original ship Conte Rosso. Wang Chonghui also went north on the same ship. He said that he would stay in Shanghai to treat his nasal disease. Zhengting said that our country has decided to participate in the next Olympics and will continue to train talents. As for whether East Asian peace can be maintained for four years, it is not something to be counted on. Dai Jitao is now going to India to worship Buddha and will return before the 16th. After arriving in the motherland, I have to meet with Chiang to discuss when to go to the United States, which is not yet determined. Li Huitang said that I originally intended to give up playing football, but this path is too attractive to me, and I am afraid I cannot control myself. Shanghai said that I am a professional athlete. Due to the advice of the Sports Association, I will not make any statement at this time. When the time comes, this matter will be clear. The reason for the failure of football in the Olympics is that there were no more games from the Mumbai competition until Berlin, which led to unfamiliarity with the game and allowed the British team to take advantage. Wang Yuzeng said that the reasons for the failure of basketball were fatigue from traveling, weak physique, and stage fright. The famous football players Four Knights and Yang Shuiyi continue to play for South China. Huang Jiliang is unwilling to come out again, and Bao Jiaping is undecided.

First China Association Small Ball League: Financial Report 125

The Chinese Small Ball Association announced that the first China Association League, organized by the Chinese Small Ball Association, has now concluded. The first organizational structure and details of the Association are recorded to serve as a review for those who promote sports.

Reasons for Initiation

The association was initiated by Xu Buyun and Wu Zhenxiang, both football stars, and Huang Yifei, a satirical artist. The principle was that the promotion of small ball in West Shanghai had caused a national sensation, but unfortunately, it was destroyed by traitors in the football world. Therefore, the three gentlemen saw this and, considering the football world in West Shanghai, prepared to organize to remove the stain on the history of small ball.

Various Obstacles

On July 16th, advertisements were placed to start registration. At that time, local thugs spread malicious rumors to disrupt the association. As a result, the association had to give up the football field borrowed from the China Industrial Factory. A few days later, an article titled "False Name to Collect Money" appeared in a certain newspaper, alluding to the matter. Mr. Wu and others simply laughed it off and continued their work. The Weiguang Sports Dining Hall was negotiated for the football field, but the terrain there was low and hindered by heavy rain. Subsequently, the White Cat football field was borrowed for the event. Various difficulties were felt at the time. Helplessly, the competition entered the first football field in West Shanghai. Two weeks later, damage to the goalposts occurred. The above facts are the circumstances leading up to the conclusion.

Total Revenue

Nineteen teams participated. The regulations only charged a registration fee, and no deposit was required. Therefore, the revenue was: Zhiyi Team 2 yuan, Kang Team 2 yuan, Kanghua Team 2 yuan, Xinghua two groups 4 yuan, Meiguang Team 2 yuan, Xi Yao Team 2 yuan, Beixing Team 2 yuan, Ganyou Team 2 yuan, Hua Team 2 yuan, Leshang Team 2 yuan, Yu Yu Team 2 yuan, Gongyi Team 2 yuan, Wan Wanwei 2 yuan, Hade Team 2 yuan, Huying Team 2 yuan, Weiguang Team 2 yuan. The Weiguang local team withdrew, and the Ya Kang Team, etc., both had their registration fees returned. The total revenue was 34 yuan.

Expenditure Items

Accounting books 8 cents, writing brush 20 cents, stamp tax 20 cents, stationery and envelopes 1.29 yuan, tent fee 2 yuan, field repair fee 2 yuan, submission fee 4.26 yuan, wire bamboo basket 1 yuan, tea 30 cents, broom 20 cents, postage 50 cents, lime 60 cents, field rental fee 8 yuan, totaling 32.73 yuan.
