Soviet Swimmer Completes 59-Kilometer Long-Distance Swim 129

TASS, September 3rd, Sochi Dispatch: Soviet athletes Kuznetsov and Leicheng have completed a long-distance swimming record off the coast of the Caucasus. Kuznetsov, a student at the Moscow Sports School, used the breaststroke to cover 59.4 kilometers, lasting 28 hours and 35 minutes. Leicheng is an engineer at the Leningrad Commercial Port, swimming 56 kilometers, staying in the water five minutes longer than Kuznetsov. During the swim, they consumed meat soup and black coffee on the surface.

A storm suddenly arose on the second day of swimming, and the judges immediately ordered the swimming to stop. The swimmers were all taken aboard ships, although they were reluctant to stop swimming. Afterwards, doctors examined them and proved that their pulses were normal and their bodies were healthy.

Record of the World Games Delegation's Accompanying Journey, Letter 16, Special Correspondent of the Central News Agency, Feng Youzhen 130

In the past two months, Guangdong and Guangxi have used the excuse of resisting Japan to mobilize troops and cause disturbances. However, this has been opposed by national public opinion and Guangdong generals. The Guangdong issue has been resolved peacefully very quickly. This proves that Chinese soldiers now have a sense of unity and are not subject to the coercion of a few ambitious individuals. This reminds us of many historical lessons of unity against foreign enemies. In the second half of the eighteenth century, the German princes were unable to cooperate because some of the princes wanted to obtain interests on the right bank of the Rhine. During the Basel Peace Negotiations in 1795, the left bank of the Rhine was ceded to France. From then on, Germany's national power declined. In 1806, Napoleon disregarded everything and organized the Rhine Confederation. The confederation not only included the areas on both sides of the Rhine within its scope, but also included Bayern, Baden, Württemberg, and Hessen. Almost one-third of Germany's land was occupied. Under the pressure of Napoleon's power, Prussia had no power to resist. The crisis of the Germanic nation at that time was no different from that of China today. However, after the efforts and calls of Arndt, Fichte, Jahn, and others, the German people's national consciousness gradually awakened, and they realized the necessity of unity. Therefore, there was the victory of the Wars of Liberation and the Austro-Prussian War of 1866. Later, after Bismarck's efforts to strengthen unity, such as the success of unifying North Germany and the Customs Union, there was the victory of the Franco-Prussian War of 1871. What lessons can we learn from this? It is that if Germany had not had the loud calls of Arndt, Fichte, and Jahn, the German people might not have awakened and united so quickly. Without the unity at that time, there would not have been the victory of the Wars of Liberation and the war against Austria. Without Bismarck's success in unifying North Germany and the Customs Union, there would not have been the victory of the Franco-Prussian War of 1871. Dear students, historical facts tell us that when a country is in a time of crisis and does not want to perish, there is indeed no second way to save the country other than unity. This is true for a country, and on a smaller scale, student groups must also be united in order to have a glorious future. Overseas students are intellectuals who have received higher education. Now that they are in a foreign land, they are more deeply stimulated than ordinary citizens. Therefore, they should be the first to implement and guide this effort for unity. The association has been established for three years. During these three years, especially in the last year, it can be said that there have been no significant achievements. In this solemn opening ceremony, I hope that everyone will follow the purpose stated in our founding manifesto, to learn from each other and connect emotionally, and move towards the goal of victory on the road to national salvation through unity.

Constitution of the Federation

The constitution of the Federation was passed at the founding meeting and revised again at the current annual meeting. The full text is recorded as follows: Article 1: This association is named "Federation of Chinese Students Unions in Europe," with the English name Federation of Chinese Students Unions in Europe. Article 2: The purpose of this association is: (1) To seek the interests of Chinese students in Europe; (2) To enhance the mutual relationship among members; (3) To study various issues related to our country; (4) To contribute opinions to the country and promote the culture of the motherland. Article 3: Membership qualifications: (1) Full members: Chinese student associations in European countries that can represent the majority of students, with the introduction of one country and the approval of two-thirds of the executive committee, can become full members of the current session, enjoy the right to elect workers of the association, and send two representatives as executive members of the association. However, each country can only participate in the association with one student union. (2) Honorary members: Compatriots who enthusiastically support the association, with the introduction of one country and the approval of two-thirds of the executive committee, can become honorary members of the association. Article 4: Rights: All full members of the association enjoy the following rights: (1) Right to elect (2) Right to be elected (3) Right to propose (4) Right to vote. Honorary members of the association do not have the above rights. Article 5: Obligations: All members of the association have the obligation to abide by the constitution of the association and the resolutions of the general meeting. Those who violate this may have their membership suspended for a considerable period with the approval of more than two-thirds of the executive committee. Article 6: Organization: After the closing of the general meeting of the association, the executive committee is organized by two representatives sent by each country to manage the affairs of the association. The executive committee elects one committee member from one country to be in charge of routine affairs as well as secretarial and accounting duties. The term of office is set for one year and must be rotated among the countries. Article 7: General Meeting: The association holds an annual meeting once a year, held in the country where the standing committee is located. Article 8: Funds: The association's funds are divided into two types: (1) Annual fee: Each full member of the country must pay an annual fee of eight pounds. In special circumstances, with the consent of two-thirds of the executive committee, it may be reduced. (2) Free donation: The association may solicit donations from members or accept external donations when necessary. Article 9: All resolutions of the association must be approved by two-thirds of the members before they can be passed. Article 10: The association cannot be dissolved without the unanimous decision of all members. Article 11: This constitution cannot be amended without the proposal of more than one-third of the members and the approval of more than two-thirds of the general meeting. Article 12: This constitution shall take effect from the date of formal establishment of the association. (End of text)

List of Departments for National Agencies to Admit Overseas Students in the 23rd Year 134

In the past, provinces and cities directly selected and sent students who were deemed qualified for overseas study by the provincial and municipal education departments. The Ministry of Education only made an endorsement on the report. Since the Ministry of Education stipulated the re-examination method in the 22nd year, students selected by various provinces and cities must undergo a re-examination by the Ministry of Education. If the re-examination results were not good, they would not be allowed to study abroad. In the 23rd year, the re-examination was changed to review, but it was difficult to leave the country if the review deemed that the results were not good. This is the general situation of the Ministry of Education's serious handling of the selection of overseas students by various provinces and cities in recent years. According to investigations, a total of 79 overseas students were admitted by national agencies in the 23rd year, including 21 from the education departments of Jiangsu (2), Anhui (3), Hunan (3), Hubei (2), Shanxi (re-examination not admitted), Chahar (2), Guangxi (4), and Guangdong (5) provinces (hereinafter, education departments will be abbreviated as departments), 30 from the China-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Board of Trustees (hereinafter abbreviated as the Fund Board), 4 from the National Tsinghua University (hereinafter abbreviated as Tsinghua University), and 4 from the National Central Research Institute and other agencies (hereinafter abbreviated as the Research Institute and others). Shen Bao Literature and Art Special Issue

On the Wharf of the Sanitation Company 145

— Ouyang Shan

After exchanging the bill of lading for cash at the accounting office of the Guangzhou Sanitation Company, the farmer Cao Jin came out. The Pearl River returned from the distant sea, flashing dazzling golden light, carrying the most urgent tune, turning up the floating yellow mud from the bottom of the river,挟着 various shells and animals, discolored seaweed, and waste discarded by humans, flowing back into the vast fields. It was like a pure gold, huge, and poisonous snake. Its whole body was bulging, and bubbles were emerging from every small pore on its snake skin. The river surface within fifteen miles was filled with the salty morning sea breeze, vigorous, making the people of Guangzhou more courageous than yesterday.

Shamian floated on the riverbank like a mud turtle, its back covered with green moss from distant years. The gray tiled houses on both banks faced each other from afar, and towering above them were the stone buildings of the customs house. The customs house clock chimed with a heavy, leisurely metallic sound, and the whistle of the steamship in the river was like the cries of a child. The bricks and mud in front of the embankments on both sides were the first to get wet, and soon they were completely submerged in the water.

Here, on the opposite bank, in the river, accompanied by various sounds, Guangzhou's daily song of labor began. It seemed to be like this:

"Yesterday has passed, follow us...

Today, we are building a happy place without deception in the whole world,

Follow us!"

Cao Jin's younger brother, Cao Hai, was sitting on a dung boat. As soon as he saw his brother, he stood up swaying at the stern of the boat. The small boat was tied under the wharf at the front, impacted by the river water, resolutely using its pointed head to emerge towards the shore.

They spoke in excessively loud voices:

"How many loads did you buy?" the person on the boat asked.

"A total of twenty-five loads," the kind brother replied, gesturing with his hands.

"A lot!"

"Not much!"

"Can you handle it?"

"You want to slack off again!"

The person on the boat saw his brother's satisfied and happy face, so he said nothing and sat down again at the stern of the boat.

Cao Jin sat on a large rock on the bank, surrounded by a wide mudflat. He used a piece of broken tile to draw ridges of fields under his feet, writing words like "bumper harvest of five grains" or "peace for people and livestock" in each grid. The gray-white red hair cement road leading from the Sanitation Company's dung wharf to the pier reflected the strong sunlight on his forehead.

Sun Yongchang, the Sanitation Company's accountant, walked towards the farmer with gecko-like steps. He was a greedy idler, around forty years old, and his extremely wrinkled face made people suspect that he was constantly taking some kind of bitter medicine.

As he walked, he thought: "Tenants are all stupid animals—but why can money be made from them? Hmph, idiots! When they take out the money, they always pretend to be reluctant and stingy, but in the end, they always take out the cash without adding or subtracting!"

He asked Cao Jin with great contempt:

"Have you corrected your thinking?"

"What thinking of mine?"

"Ai—!" His voice rose from low to high, with an unnatural tremor. "Don't you often say? You say: the government doesn't care about anything!"

"Yes. Isn't it?"

Cao Jin said, looking at Sun Yongchang warily. That face had nothing but wrinkles, but it seemed to reveal a kind of aura—which was common among Guangzhou's tax merchants and donation thugs, who thought they were managing the taxpayers for the government. Sun Yongchang swept his bitter eyes over the rolling Pearl River, where small boats carrying various goods crawled like ants. If he wanted to teach the stupid farmer Cao Jin, he thought this was the perfect time.

"How can you say that, my dung brother?"

"Just talk about the price of fertilizer, please don't blame me," Cao Jin replied humbly, not prepared to anger the accountant Sun Yongchang. "You raised the price, and it's still your own decision."

"But you're talking nonsense. Why is raising the fertilizer price our own decision? No one can do anything the government doesn't allow."

Sun Yongchang stared at the pier, where many small boats were pushed and squeezed by the river water, creaking loudly. Idle boatmen curled up their feet and dozed off in the sunlight, Cao Jin stretched out his fingers and calculated:

"One three-fen-six (Guangdong currency, five cents in silver)... another three-fen-six... Uncle Chang, I'm not complaining to you, how much is a load of manure worth—how can we bear such a price increase? It seems that the government listens to you very much. If you manage us—things will naturally not go well."

"Good stuff! Good stuff! You'll rebel soon! I dare to bet."

Accountant Sun Yongchang left Cao Jin, leaving the honest tenant alone on a tile and mud square bisected by a red cement path, and walked to the shore himself. The Pearl River roared unhappily, and a huge sound of the tide biting the shore came from somewhere. It shook its golden, shimmering body, warning Sun Yongchang, roaring like a beast, telling him not to get close to it.

Why wouldn't Sun Yongchang let himself please others?——While the accountant was walking by the pier, scolding the boatmen one by one, Cao Jin was thinking about such questions. People could assume that Sun Yongchang was a clumsy businessman who didn't know how to do business. Many customers came from the countryside with cash to the provincial capital to buy fertilizer that others thought was just waste—what kind of business was this? But Sun Yongchang didn't like any of his customers. As if this was also a funny thing, Cao Jin smiled sweetly.

After Sun Yongchang had expressed his hatred for the boatmen (which was actually like his dissatisfaction with all of humanity), he turned back to Cao Jin and said:

"You are a silly bird! You've been poisoned by your brother—will he have a good death! Everything in the world is managed by someone, and the government manages everyone. This wharf, these boats, these bastards, don't they all need to be managed well? If everyone messes up, what will this world become!"

There was a person Cao Jin had to find at the Sanitation Company's wharf, he was the wharf gangster Big Snake Head Wang Deshan. This person managed five wharves according to a kind of habit. They were arranged one after another along the Pearl River, standing, staring blankly at the ever-drying river center, as if they themselves were slowly sinking day by day. Their wooden feet were gnawed and rubbed, growing slippery green moss, but some feet were exceptionally thin, as if the flesh above had already been removed, leaving delicate, almost broken bone tubes.

Wang Deshan divided the ruling power of these five wharves with the Guangzhou Municipal Government with his powerful influence. The porters above could only get work under his orders, and no goods could be shipped without his consent.

"Bring the money..." He said to the cargo owner. After getting the money, he shouted loudly to his subordinates: "Come two people! Are you all dead!" This rude and careless Big Snake Head often only said such words, and after ordering, he ran away. He didn't care about things, and didn't know who he should thank—this "person" gave him power, territory, and subjects.

Cao Jin was looking everywhere on the Sanitation Company's wharf. There were no goods or buildings blocking his view here, just a flat black earth by the river. There was no Wang Deshan, nor a porter. He turned into the Sanitation Company's accounting room.

"Why aren't the goods being shipped yet?" the accountant Sun Yongchang asked.

Cao Jin pointed to the glass window and replied,

"Look, it's quiet outside... Do the goods have feet themselves?"

Sun Yongchang suggested that if he could give him six cents, then he would allow him to ship the goods himself in the name of the accounting room. What kind of nonsense could Wang Deshan negotiate with the accounting room.

"This is an illegal thing!" Cao Jin said. But he gladly accepted Sun Yongchang's proposal. In this way, that unfortunate day began with the thing that the wharf people called "stealing."

When the two brothers started to remove the twenty-five loads of manure, Big Snake Head Wang Deshan came from the rice wharf with eight brothers. "That's Cao Jin!" He jumped up and ran over, and everyone followed him. They started to beat the two brothers—the two farmers who were easily fooled anywhere. The younger brother Cao Hai was the first to be knocked unconscious and thrown unconscious on his own small boat. The older brother Cao Jin had a rib broken by a bamboo pole, crawled under the glass window of the accounting room, and lay there groaning. Accountant Sun Yongchang walked slowly to the window with the satisfying feeling of walking out of the theater. A ghostly human head immediately appeared on the window. He raised his hand inside and tapped on the glass of the window, tapped a few times and then tapped a few times, trying to call Cao Jin, who was seriously injured and lying under the eaves outside the room, to open his eyes. He saw Cao Jin open his mouth wide, his face losing color due to pain, trembling all over, but he couldn't hear him shouting anything.

Cao Jin opened his eyes, but couldn't see anything, so he moved his head numbly from side to side.

"Your luck is really bad, poor fool! Why did you... wait until Big Snake Head came back to ship the goods... Not too late, not too early, he came just in time—you really have no luck! …Hey, how are you now? Can't stand up and walk? Then what are you going to do?"

Constantly knocking on the glass window inside, Accountant Sun Yongchang repeatedly said the above words to the "thief" outside who was gradually losing consciousness.

Terror 146

— TK

The Little Boat of Life 147

— Chu Yang

Misty night,

Boundless black sea,

I float on the sea in

The little boat of life!

Lost my direction...

The floating lights flicker.

This is a sea of nothingness!

Everything seems to be dead...

The Radio has lost its magical power,

I can no longer shout,

I can't even cry,

Isolated and helpless, who will save me?

Sink down...sink down...

Terrible bottomless abyss!

This is a daydream of life:

The goddess of love has broken her wings

Standing remotely on the extinguished lighthouse,

Wearing a light white lotus dress,

She gazes at me from afar in despair,

Gazes at me, I can't see her expression clearly,

Her face is whiter than the lotus...

I shout with a hoarse voice:

The tape of thought rushes out of my fragile skull,

—Where are you going?

There is no easy road in this world,

In the black sea, there is only sinking, you cannot stay;

Raise your sail again,

Beat your oars, row, row, row...

Hold the balance of the rudder of life,

Row forward forever towards the dawn!

It's Orange and Tangerine Season Again 148

— Chen Zizhan

"Remember the best scenery of the year, it's orange and tangerine season again."

Now the domestic oranges and tangerines are about to ripen. According to Han Yanzhi's Citrus Spectrum in the Song Dynasty, there are true tangerines, branch-grown tangerines, sea red tangerines, Dongting tangerines, sweet tangerines, wood tangerines, vermilion tangerines, and steamed bun tangerines. Oranges include yellow oranges, vermilion oranges, green oranges, milk oranges, collapsed oranges, sand oranges, wrapped oranges, cotton oranges, early yellow oranges, and lychee oranges. Nowadays, people generally only know that tangerines include the edible Shantou ponkan and snow tangerine, Xiamen banana tangerine, and the inedible stinky-skin tangerine; oranges are named after their place of origin, such as Guangzhou orange, Dongting orange, and Huangyan honey orange. The Citrus Spectrum says, "Tangerines and oranges come from Suzhou, Taizhou, west from Jingzhou, south from Yue, Guang, and Fuzhou, but those from Wenzhou are the best." As far as I personally see, Wenzhou oranges contain a bitter taste, and although they are said to be sweet in bitterness, they may not be considered top quality. Li Shizhen's Herbal Compendium says: "Tangerines are southern fruits, and they are abundant in Min, Guang, Wen, Tai, Su, and Fuzhou, and Jingzhou. Although they exist in Sichuan, they are not as good." That's right, tangerines and oranges are southern fruits. The northern climate is cold and not suitable for tangerines and oranges. Even if they are planted, they will mutate. Broadly speaking, the north and south of our country are divided by the Huai River in terms of soil and climate. It is not suitable to plant oranges north of the Huai River, so the ancients had the saying "an orange becomes a trifoliate orange when it crosses the Huai River." The further south you go, the sweeter the oranges become, so Guangzhou oranges can be considered the king of oranges in our country. Of course, the warm climate in Guangdong plays a big role in this.

Chinese loquats and oranges mostly ripen and are picked in the late autumn and winter. Once spring arrives, oranges will rot. Traditional methods of storage can only preserve the outside appearance, and the inside is either dry and shriveled or moldy, which is exactly what is meant by "golden and jade on the outside, rotten cotton on the inside." It is not easy to find good oranges to eat between spring and summer. Since the opening of the seas, American oranges have been imported, so you don't have to worry about not having oranges to eat all year round as long as you live in a major city and have money. However, in Europe and the United States, some people have already found them too expensive and can't afford to eat them, so they eat tomatoes instead, so tomatoes are called "poor man's oranges." There is also a saying: "A home with tomatoes has no sick people." It turns out that tomatoes are the most vitamin-rich fruit, especially vitamin A, which is eight times more abundant than oranges. Therefore, tomatoes are regarded as an indispensable nourishing food in European and American countries, equivalent to oranges, and the output is large and the price is low, which is more cost-effective than eating oranges. Tomatoes have been imported into our country for only about forty or fifty years, which is comparable to the import of American oranges. Not many people plant them, and few people like to eat them. Because of the scarcity, they are sometimes more expensive than oranges. Only in summer and autumn, when the output is higher, are they cheaper. I don't know about other places, but in Shanghai, the market price of tomatoes and American oranges is roughly the same. I have suffered from stomach problems for twenty years, and my wife has also had intestinal problems for several years. Her intestines were operated on, and it has been three years now, and she still cannot eat hard rice. Now, both she and I have to eat oranges every day, and she also needs to drink tomato soup. These two things have become our daily necessities, and also luxuries. For the past three years, we have felt that these two things are a huge expense.

My wife's intestinal disease, according to the doctor, "is a severe form of tuberculosis, and this section of the intestine must be removed." My wife did not dare to take the risk, and I could not force her. The doctor initially said that she could only live for half a year, and after half a year passed, he said that she could only live for one year. Now that three years have passed, the doctor says, "Her resistance is particularly strong, and she is well-cared for." Alas! Living in a home like ours, can we say that she is well-cared for? Dragging a large group of wild horse-like children, living in a cramped alley house in a big city, where sunlight is not enough and the air is not fresh enough, chicken soup cannot be eaten every day, and nutritious food relies only on oranges and tomatoes, and we often worry about the lack of them. However, she is able to eat these two things often, which seems to have had a great effect, so she is still alive today, which is a stroke of luck. Recently, I read the 126th issue of the Chinese Medical Journal, and saw Hou Xiangchuan's article "The Relationship between Vitamin C and Disease," which said:

Clausen, S.W., has elaborated on the close relationship between vitamin C deficiency in guinea pigs and tuberculosis. Although the results obtained by most researchers are not very similar, most of them have reduced the symptoms of tuberculosis patients by injecting vitamin C. McConkey M. and Smith, D.t. reported the results of their research, using seventy-two adult guinea pigs, feeding them with the sputum of tuberculosis patients every day, for six weeks to four months, of which twenty-seven guinea pigs suffered from intestinal tuberculosis due to a slight deficiency of vitamin C. The remaining guinea pigs were fed the same food, with an adequate amount of vitamin C added, and only two suffered from intestinal tuberculosis. It can be concluded that vitamin C has the effect of protecting guinea pigs from tuberculosis. Schagan, B., has stated that when there is a lack of vitamin C, there will be more cases of scurvy, and cases of tuberculosis will also increase at the same time.

Mr. Hou also has an article "Vitamin C in Chinese Citrus and its Processed Products," which says that he used chemical and biological methods to measure the juice of forty kinds of citrus fruits, and proved that the vitamin C content of Shatin pomelo and grapefruit is the highest, followed by snow tangerine, then various grapefruits, and various oranges, and the lowest is Taizhou honey orange, local orange, and Huangyan and Quantai Mountain honey orange. He also believes that Shantou honey orange (also known as ponkan) has the same ability to resist scurvy as American oranges. And Guangzhou orange or Shantou snow tangerine is even better than American oranges. Since oranges are the fruit with the most vitamin C, and whether a person lacks vitamin C is closely related to scurvy and tuberculosis, which has been scientifically proven. Then, my wife, who is suffering from intestinal tuberculosis, has arrived at this time of oranges and tangerines, shouldn't she be happy?

(Written on September 27, 1936. The title is "More on Oranges." An article "On Oranges" was published in Shen Bao's Free Talk.)

Night Market Portraits 149

— Simu

As the colorful, fiery flames of neon lights begin to burn, flickering, flowing, swirling, appearing and disappearing, chasing, leaping, the various "night shops" lining the sidewalks create a "vaudeville" of the metropolis, and the show begins.

Hesitantly, slowly moving—no, a mass of people pushing, shoving, squeezing, and crowding, the audience, stares at one stall after another.

The clatter of wooden clogs is buried in the surging torrent of hawking cries, in the eddies of popular songs from the radio. The vivid colors of women's kimonos and makeup, like the lights, dazzle and pierce the eyes. The old, shiny black uniforms of university students, and the foreign-style light-colored cheongsams of Chinese female students also weave through the dance of color and light.

Cloth stalls, clothing stalls, used goods stalls, book stalls, toy stalls, "roasted cuttlefish" tents, flower girls without stalls—the "night market" can satisfy all the large and small needs indispensable to urban life, and even create new needs for you.

"Memory booster! Memory booster!..." A small, mustached man with gleaming eyes splashes spittle as he advertises, his stall also displaying a sign that reads "Recommended by Dr. So-and-so, Professor So-and-so."

A few steps away, a female stall vendor is busy tearing and washing old socks, muttering to herself. It turns out she is selling something called "no-thread" sock-mending paste.

With a "crack," the vendor selling "garden clogs" (low clogs worn in the yard), in a showy manner, desperately throws his goods to the ground. A small woman in Western clothes, who has just walked by, is startled and mutters under her breath, "What an idiot!"

Surrounded by many people, a man selling saws is sawing wood with all his might. There are already quite a few pieces of sawn wood and sawdust. The smiling audience seems to pay the most attention to the large, soybean-sized, stinking sweat on his dirty forehead and bare black arms.

The gaps in the night market are filled by a group of "freelancers."

Six or seven "street portrait artists" (excuse my use of such a realistic term!) stand in a row on the side of the department store, soliciting business, displaying their various signs—no, their works of art—which all seem to have a bit of a caricature flavor. Their own thin, pale, bony faces, paired with hair that looks like a handful of straw, or overly large black glasses that have slipped down to the tips of their noses, a French-style torn hat tilted on their heads, or a maroon-colored Turkish fez, and the inspired gaze and gestures they use when capturing the models and customers they have caught and painting on the spot—all of this constitutes an excellent living caricature. It is not they themselves who are being satirized, but they themselves are satirizing.

Adjacent to them are several fortune-telling stalls, with refined, scholarly-style vendors wearing black outer robes, and paper lanterns on their tables decorated with trigrams and lit candles, imprinting a "historical anachronism" on this modern metropolitan night. However, the person who is intently holding out his palm to be examined by a tall, elegant old fortune-teller happens to be a young man in a university student uniform. This symbol seems even more meaningful.

A mummy-like beggar standing on the remaining one leg, a capitalist among beggars sitting in a two-wheeled cart wearing a copper gong hat that obscures his eyes and nose, and a yellow dog kneeling in front of him with a money basket hanging around his neck—these essential but insignificant characters in this urban "new vaudeville"—have also made their appearance. When they reach this corner, the pedestrians' feet stop for a moment, but they are not looking at the beggars, but at the begging dog. These few lowest-level "freelancers" are inserted precisely between the street artists and the street metaphysicians, and perhaps someone will suddenly have the whimsical idea that this also symbolizes their mutual destined connection?

The flames of the neon lights burn more fiercely, and the movements of the pedestrian audience become more sluggish. That is precisely the moment when the street theater is "full." Famous stars of the play, put forth a little more effort before you starve!

Tomorrow there will be another night market; but tomorrow—who knows about tomorrow!

The Story of Confucius Being Deprived of Food 150

— Jieren

I once talked about an interesting story in a newspaper supplement, which roughly said:

When Confucius was deprived of food in Chen, he took his two disciples, Yan Hui and Zhong You, to the street one day and saw a shop selling yuanxiao (sweet dumplings), with a sign saying: "Sweet bean paste filled yuanxiao, one for one 'wen' (ancient Chinese coin)." Confucius asked Yan Hui if he had any money. Yan Hui replied, "I never have any money." He then asked Zhong You, who said, "I only have one 'wen'." Confucius said, "That's how we can do it!" So he took out a pen from his pocket and added a stroke to the "one" character on the sign, turning it into a "ten" character.

The three of them swaggered in and ate ten yuanxiao in total. Zhong You took out his one 'wen' and threw it on the table. The waiter asked, "Is this a small account?" They angrily said, "Is there a small account for eating snacks!" Of course, the waiter did not admit that this was the price of the yuanxiao, so they started arguing. Confucius told them to bring the sign in to see, and sure enough, "one 'wen' for one" had become "one 'wen' for ten." The yuanxiao shop owner apologized and said, "Fortunately, you met us today, because we scholars do things with conscience and reason. Otherwise, if you added a stroke above the head of the 'ten' character, it would be even worse."

This resolved the matter. As they were leaving, Confucius solemnly said to the yuanxiao shop owner, "Fortunately, you met us today, because we scholars do things with conscience and reason. Otherwise, if you added a stroke above the head of the 'ten' character, it would be even worse."

Regardless of the truth of the story, this is an excellent satire. Defrauding someone else of their yuanxiao and still saying that it is "with conscience and reason," isn't that a portrayal of a certain type of person? However, they only resorted to that fraudulent means because they were too poor to eat. This kind of thing is also very common. Don't you see university students becoming robbers and thieves?

When a person is threatened by material things, it will force them to disregard propriety, justice, integrity, and shame, and do things that they would not otherwise be willing to do. The instinct to survive is the innate ability of humans and all animals. If you prevent them from continuing to survive, they will naturally struggle to seek the continuation of their survival. If they were not so poor, they would not have cheated others out of their yuanxiao to eat. Everyone has some self-esteem. It's just like when they cheated others out of their yuanxiao, they still covered it up by saying that it was "with conscience and reason." A thief would never be willing to do that when people are starving.

How to enable everyone to continue their survival is a very important issue. This issue must be resolved. Talking about anything else while ignoring this issue is in vain. But it requires everyone's continuous efforts. It is not an impossible thing. Hasn't one place already completed this difficult task? And by then, Confucius would definitely not cheat others out of their yuanxiao to eat.

Stepping on the Shores of My Homeland 151

— Xiangshan

When I was very close to Wusong, I saw the yellow sea current; here I smelled the breath of the mainland.

In the welcome song, the ship slowly docked, and at this time the people on the pier who came to meet us raised their hats and handkerchiefs; excited and nervous.

Outside the ship, it was drizzling.

When the ship lowered the gangplank, countless porters surged in. In the clamor of these porters, I felt a kind of intimacy. This intimacy was the intimacy of the native language of my homeland.

The language is full of richness and warmth, and it contains the golden stories of my childhood. In my teens of travel life; I haven't heard the language of my hometown for a long time. Northern language, even foreign languages ​​- in these emotionless languages, I feel lonely and lonely; but today I hear the same language as my hometown spoken from the mouths of the porters, and the attachment and intimacy that I feel are difficult to describe.

Ah! This language is telling the golden dream of childhood in the midst of vastness.

Poor myself, how long will I be able to immerse myself in this local language? When the sky is cloudless in September, won't I be returning to a foreign country? Won't I be leaving this lovely language again? Not only will I not be able to hear the sound of this language, but I will even have to suppress the sound of its utterance and use another language?

In the drizzle, I waited for my luggage to be transported out of the cabin, and on the other hand, I seemed to be absorbed in the rhythm of the native language, which sounded like a oriole singing.

If either party softens slightly, the rebound will be significant; otherwise, it will be difficult to say. Yesterday's situation was that at the opening in the morning, selling was the strongest. Large numbers of No. 4, No. 5, No. 10, and No. 11 were sold off. Although there were occasional buybacks, selling was still the majority, especially the selling of No. 11 was the most lively. The market price fell again, suddenly by half a yuan to about one yuan. People's confidence was diminished, and they were quite panicked. In the second session, No. 375 turned from buying to selling, and the market atmosphere felt heavily pressured. Retail investors also sold off one after another, falling another 0.12 to 0.45 yuan. In the afternoon, rumors were rampant in the local area, and short sellers gloated over the disaster, not hesitating to exaggerate. The market atmosphere was even more discouraged. No. 10 and No. 11 frantically sold off, even more so than before. The decline intensified, with the two falling sharply by 0.9 yuan, and the rest also falling by 0.45 to 0.75 yuan. At closing, it was rumored that diplomatic channels were not exhausted and that there was a trend toward normalcy. People's sentiment turned stable. No. 4 and No. 11 saw more buying than selling, and No. 47 also saw buying. No. 31 suddenly had a large number of short covering, so although the previous ones continued to fall by 0.12 to 0.65 yuan, the latter ones suddenly turned to rise. This month's Class B was raised by No. 31 by as much as 0.7 yuan. However, the long-term Class A was still weak. If the news is not widespread, people will inevitably be confused again. The market price resulted in Class E this month falling the most by 1.85 yuan, and Class B this month falling the least by 1 yuan. Today's market conditions must be extremely chaotic. The total number of transactions was about 16 million yuan. The result of its rise and fall is compared and listed on the left (unit: yuan, transaction unit: 100 yuan).

Yarn and Cloth: The Yarn Market Suddenly Sees a Miserable Fall; The Environment is Poor, and Long Positions Turn to Selling; Each Month Falls by a Huge 3-4 Yuan 156

The yarn market, which had been rising for days, suddenly reported a miserable fall yesterday. This situation is entirely due to the speculation of general speculators. The reason for its sharp decline is that it has risen by 18 yuan compared to the low price. Recently, various parties have purchased yarn, with about 20,000 bales. Customers' appetites seem to be full, so long positions have sold off one after another, and the market has fallen more and more sharply. The exchange's chips for Jin Cheng, Shuang Lu, and Xing Shi brands of yarn fell sharply by 3 to 5 yuan.

The Marked Yarn Market Atmosphere is Extremely Loose and Abusive

The marked yarn pre-market opening saw each month presenting a downward trend, and was also shrouded in a bad atmosphere. People were panicked, and large investors sold off, so the market's chips were loose and abusive. Therefore, the market gradually went downstream, and the falling trend was very strong, because general floating long positions,鉴于the bad situation, were particularly keen on cutting positions, and the market became increasingly unsupported. It was noted that Ming De He Xing Da Chang Cheng Xin Hua and other long positions sold off in large quantities, while Tong Ji Da Feng Da Fu Geng Feng Tai Chang Chang Feng Xin Cheng and other short positions replenished even more. As a result, each month's marked yarn fell by 1.6 to 2.5 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. The market atmosphere was very fearful after the afternoon opening. Because the securities and gold gangs came to sell off together, the falling trend became even more severe. The second and third sessions were still sluggish. By the time of closing, because the degree of decline was too great, it triggered a slight rebound in covering. As a result, May fell by another 0.7 to 0.9 yuan compared to the morning closing price. It was noted that the sell-off included Ming De 3000 bales, He Xing 5050 bales, Sen Kang 3150 bales, Chang Yu 1900 bales, Feng Tai 2000 bales, Wang Tai Xing 2900 bales, Da Chang Cheng 4300 bales, Xin Hua 1350 bales, Yu Da 6000 bales, Ming Hua 1800 bales, Shen Ji 1800 bales. The buy-in included Zheng Ji 2150 bales, Da Fu 1050 bales, Tong Ji 1650 bales, Da Feng 1750 bales, Yuan Da 1650 bales, Geng Feng 4100 bales, Tai Chang 4050 bales, Chang Feng 8050 bales, Bai Cheng 3500 bales, Lan Kang 1350 bales. The highest and lowest market prices for the day are listed on the left.

Spot Yarn Selling Prices Also See a Sharp Fall

The spot yarn sales are still good. It was noted that all gangs bought a total of 1220 bales throughout the day. The selling prices of yarn fell by 2 to 4 yuan. The amounts handled by each gang are as follows.

Sellers Swarm in; The Cotton Market Cannot Support 157

The cotton market fell sharply due to the yarn market's decline. Moreover, the weather was sunny and right, and the situation of new cotton was excellent. According to people in the industry, the future is estimated to still have a hope of increasing, so some people tended to sell off, and the market turned downward. However, the overseas cotton industry situation is still good.

Marked Cotton Falls Sharply by 5-6 Jiao

The marked cotton pre-market opening was due to the continuous rise of American cotton, about 17 pounds in two days. The Osaka Sanpin yarn and cotton rose by one yuan. There was a rumor of a recent squeeze, and long positions shouted very high, rising 0.3-0.4 jiao. When shooting to the long term, it turned lax. Unexpectedly, when the second session opened, the yarn market fell, the selling wind suddenly rose, and the falling trend was very strong, falling sharply by 0.4 to 0.65 jiao. The long term was挫折, and by the third closing, the market state was getting weaker and weaker. In fact, the weather was good, the new cotton production was excellent, and there were still quite a few people who sold off when it rose. It was noted that Ming De Yu Da He Xing Feng Tai Run Kang and other long positions came out in large quantities, while Chang He Hua Mao Sen Kang Tai Chang Yi Chang Yi Kang Yuan Xing Chang and other long positions continued to advance, and short positions covered. As a result, each month's marked cotton fell by 0.25 to 0.45 jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. After the afternoon opening, the situation was panicked, and the situation on the table changed sharply. Sellers swarmed in and fell sharply by 0.5 jiao, because most long positions吐出, which caused the market to be unsupported. As a result, each month fell by another 0.25 to 0.3 jiao compared to the morning closing. It was noted that the sell-off included Yu Da 15,000 dan, Ming De 15,900 dan, He Xing 8,500 dan, Geng Feng 8,800 dan, Feng Tai 7,600 dan, Tong He 4,500 dan, Run Kang 3,100 dan, Jin Chang 4,100 dan, Mao Jin Yuan Da 4,400 dan, Da Feng 3,500 dan, Tai Chang 10,100 dan, Yi Chang 3,800 dan, Yi Kang 6,900 dan, Chang He 10,400 dan, Yuan Xing Chang 7,600 dan, Chang Feng 5,500 dan, Xin Cheng 4,300 dan, Shen Chang 5,300 dan, Hua Mao 3,500 dan. Spot Cotton Factories Need Constantly

Spot cotton consumption is still not thin, and factories need it constantly. The sources are Yao flower 6,800 bales, and Tong flower 2,300 bales.

Silk and Tea Silk Market Also Returns to Stagnation 158

Yesterday, overseas silk prices showed a slight improvement, but there was still a difference of about 40 yuan compared to the prices held by Shanghai merchants, so there were still few transactions. French firms in particular rarely inquired, and foreign firms' silk sales entered a standstill. On the user side, there was a slight increase in appetite from other ports, but the local market also became sluggish due to the current situation. As a result, the Shanghai silk market, which seemed to be expanding, was momentarily stagnant.

American Cotton Supported by Liverpool Market Conditions 159

Yesterday, American cotton opened. Liverpool news was good. Foreign firms, fellow traders, and Wall Street actively bought in. Fabric demand was smooth. Prices for all months rose by seven to ten points. Subsequently, cotton farmers hedged, causing a partial correction. However, cotton farmers, after the price increase, seemed inclined to hoard. The market closed flat and weak. Spot prices rose by eight points, and futures rose by eight to ten points. British cotton spot prices rose by three points, and futures rose by seven to eight points. Indian cotton merchants and mainland exporters traded in large quantities. The amounts liquidated by bulls were absorbed. Bengal rose by 1.5 rupees, Oomra rose by 2.25 rupees, and Broach rose by 2 rupees. (Original telegram, 30th)

According to a Bombay telegram, opening predictions for the first day were: Broach at 221 rupees, up 0.75 rupees; Oomra at 198 rupees, up 0.5 rupees; Bengal at 157 rupees, up 0.25 rupees.

Piece Goods: Cotton Cloth Fluctuates with the Situation; Credit to the Interior is Already Restricted; Four Major Firms Can Barely Maintain Operations 161

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market turned weak. Overseas cotton markets were consistently strong and rising. Domestically, due to the tense situation, rumors abounded, causing widespread panic. Yarn and cotton prices fell sharply, leading to a gloomy cloth market. Eastern goods, fine cloth, and fine twill were mostly sold off according to the market. Selling prices varied due to differing opinions, generally falling by 2.5 to 5 fen per piece. However, those with shortages of spot goods still sold at the original prices. British firms like Jardine Matheson and factories producing heavy coarse cloth, due to strong sales across various regions and difficulty in delivering spot goods, again raised prices by 5 fen per piece. Heavy coarse cloth, due to large absorption by the military uniform industry, was in short supply on the market. Factory prices increased, causing market prices to rise sharply. Factories producing printed and finished cloth were arranging for deliveries, keeping the market quiet but firm. Due to the serious situation and financial tightness, loading goods was slightly sluggish. Wholesale firms on this street and credit transactions with interior regions were also strictly restricted.

Yesterday was the 3009th auction by Yuan Fang & Co., showcasing four types of goods: Western satin, velvet, wool broadcloth, and silk. Bleached cloth, foreign yarn, poplin, and red foreign gray cloth were not included. The market coincided with the passing of the Autumn Festival, nearing the winter goods season, so customers in the interior had needs to prepare. Auction prices increased more than they decreased. Of the 49 lots of various goods, totaling 79 cases, Western satin including "Xi Hu" brands saw prices rise by 1-2 fen per yard compared to the previous period. Velvet and wool broadcloth did not change much. Silk "An Dian Bao" brand increased by 1.10 yuan per piece. "Cai Ba Shi" rose by 90 sen, the most. "Five Star Three Ding Jia Yan Guo Gong" rose by 50 sen. Others rose by about 30 sen. "Hai Niu Kuai Li" and "Hai Tian Ping Ju" were flat.

Grains: Wheat Flour Bulls No Longer Intend to Persist 163

After the flour market opened yesterday morning, prices for all months fell uniformly. This was because the price of foreign wheat, as reported in Chicago, had fallen by 60-80 sen in a few days, Canada fell by 1 yuan, and Liverpool fell by about 4 pence. Therefore, at the opening, sentiment was already soft. Prices for October through December fell by 20-30 fen. January and beyond remained relatively calm. Later, as bulls gradually exited and rumors about the situation intensified, the situation gradually worsened. By the time of the afternoon opening, due to sluggish actual sales and outside bulls unwilling to strongly persist due to the situation, the market felt sluggish, falling another 10 fen compared to the morning closing. If the situation remains unstable, the market will definitely become sluggish and is likely to soften. March contracts were also auctioned. The initial price was 3.445 yuan, and the closing price was 3.44 yuan, also down 1.5 fen.

Wheat Futures Fall Inevitably 164

Yesterday, in the wheat market, when trading opened in the morning, prices fell uniformly across all months. This was because the price of foreign wheat, during the market closure, fell by 60-80 sen to 1 yuan. Therefore, prices immediately dropped by 20-30 fen. After the second session, near-term contracts showed some stability, while for far-term contracts, buyers exited and prices fell step by step. Trading volume in various months was also brisk. By the time of the afternoon opening, due to the sluggish flour market and many rumors about the situation, prices fell another 40-50 fen. The final difference was as much as 90 fen, and at least 70 fen. This situation was almost entirely driven by sentiment. High-quality wheat prices remain firm, while medium- and lower-quality wheat were soft by 20-30 fen. At the same time, it is necessary to take two types of medicines: those that nourish the nerves and those that strengthen the essence and tonify the kidneys. According to clinical experience, "Memory Neuratic" (米美爾補腦汁) is a particularly effective nerve tonic for neurasthenia. "Well Tonic" (還爾童), made from refined testicular essence, is extremely effective for strengthening essence and tonifying the kidneys. All kinds of sexual disorders caused by reproductive dysfunction can be gradually cured after taking this product.

The effectiveness and safety of these two medicines have been proven by doctors worldwide and are highly reputable. Patients who take both medicines simultaneously can surely transform from weak to strong in a very short period, regaining the joy of life.

Celebrating President Chiang's Birthday 179

— Wen

The Central Propaganda Department issued a notice stating that the 29th of this month is President Chiang Kai-shek's fiftieth birthday. In order to venerate merit and repay virtue, various regions will hold grand celebrations. Of course, we must also express our congratulations on this grand occasion.

In total, President Chiang Kai-shek has been in power for a full ten years, from the Northern Expedition in the fifteenth year of the Republic to the establishment of the capital in Nanjing. During these short ten years, China has undergone a major historical change. From the establishment of the capital in Nanjing to the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident, China's national crisis began to unfold. President Chiang Kai-shek, as the first to face this historical crisis, shouldered an extremely heavy responsibility. Therefore, on the occasion of celebrating President Chiang Kai-shek's fiftieth birthday, the only hope of the people for President Chiang Kai-shek is how to shoulder this overly heavy task, overcome this unprecedented national crisis, and save China from this losing game. This is the most essential point.

Today, the people seem to have such a desire: regardless of what form politics takes, we support it. We even support the government asking all people to sacrifice their lives, as long as the government can resolutely shoulder the responsibility of saving the national crisis. Regardless of who it is, we will unite to enthusiastically support them, giving them the most noble position in Chinese history. Regardless of what they were like in the past, as long as they can resolutely shoulder this major responsibility at any time, the people will enthusiastically support them at any time. But this great cause of saving the national crisis is not placed in the distant future, but must be realized immediately. If this can be done, anyone who can step forward to shoulder this responsibility will be the greatest hero in the history of our national rejuvenation. Looking around the country today, the only one who can take on this responsibility without hesitation is President Chiang Kai-shek. Therefore, today, as we celebrate President Chiang Kai-shek's birthday, we can only offer this most sublime and sincere hope to President Chiang Kai-shek as the greatest gift that the people can offer.

No one can deny that the entire country of China has reached a crossroads where it will either live or die, without allowing for any hesitation. As Arida of Japan said, China must decide immediately whether to submit or resist and can no longer hesitate. Our neighbors have already decided the fate of our nation for us. Do we not understand? We deeply feel that the disaster of destruction is imminent. Therefore, as we congratulate President Chiang Kai-shek on his birthday, our greatest, most urgent, and only hope is that President Chiang Kai-shek will immediately take on the great responsibility of fighting for the survival of the nation when the country is already unified!

President Chiang Kai-shek once declared that the minimum limit of concession to foreign countries is that if the enemy invades even an inch of our land, we will immediately retaliate. However, today, there is also the reality that the enemy is secretly changing the landscape of China without formally occupying land, such as the much-publicized alliance of the five provinces of North China. Regarding this disguised invasion of territory, we sincerely hope that President Chiang Kai-shek will not relax his vigilance. Finally, let us all shout in unison: Support President Chiang Kai-shek, the only hero of defending against foreign aggression and saving the country today!

Amidst the Sound of Cymbals and Drums 180

— Zou Heng

Around seven o'clock in the afternoon, the erhu downstairs stopped, and the sound of moving tables and chairs started up again. Based on past experience, I guessed that they were going to play cards again. However, this guess turned out to be wrong - instead, there was a burst of cymbals and drums.

"I won't be able to finish today's article again. See, they're doing 'wu qi' again." Old Li threw down his pen in frustration.

"This is called 'fate determined by heaven.' We have no choice but to play for a while; but it's also good to have some fun on this occasion." I pushed away the manuscript paper and walked to the window.

The house where I live is on the second floor, at the front. The landlord's family lives upstairs. Perhaps because the house is not big enough, they covered the small courtyard with a glass roof, and they eat, receive guests, and play cards

Page 18

down there. As long as we push open the window and lean down, we can get a bird's-eye view of everything.

"Look at these guys, they don't look like monks or Taoists. Maybe they're nuns?" Old Li said, pointing to the shadows of people in the light downstairs.

"No, nuns wouldn't have hair. I think they look more like Taoist priestesses." I said softly. Obviously, they heard Old Li's words. Two tousled heads looked up at us for a moment, then lowered their heads again without expression. Continuing was a series of incomprehensible chants or incantations.

The layout downstairs was also a bit different from usual; a square table was placed facing the door, with a spirit tablet made of yellow paper on the table. Because it was standing upright, I couldn't see what the words were. I guess it was "State Duke Hui ×× State Duke Spirit Tablet." On both sides of the spirit tablet were two white candles, shining with a bright orange light. In the center was a metal incense burner, with three sticks of grass incense inserted in it. Several Taoist priestesses sat around the three sides of the table. Each person held a musical instrument, drums, cymbals, small bells, and wooden fish. The first two only sounded briefly at the beginning and the end. The wooden fish and small bells seemed to be a rhythm, constantly sounding along with the rising and falling chants.

I don't know what sutras they are chanting, and even the landlord who hired them to chant the sutras probably doesn't know either. I tried my best to hear a sentence or two, but I couldn't understand a single character, so I gave up this plan. Anyway, they are "chanting sutras," and that alone will satisfy the host. Any further inquiry would be meddling.

The chanting stopped, and a burst of wailing came from the drum. It seemed to be in the room where the deceased used to live downstairs. The cries seemed to be coming from women, clear and sharp, as if they wanted to break through all spatial barriers and penetrate everyone's heart.

"Listen, the clearest one is probably the landlord's eldest daughter," Old Li said to me, leaning against the wall and listening.

"It's strange, I've never seen them have any sadness or grief at all, how can they wail like this when they cry?" He said after listening for a while.

"Those who take worldly affairs too seriously will be deceived unknowingly," I lit a cigarette and took a puff. "We who pride ourselves on being clever are often fools in their eyes. You only know that crying is an expression of human emotions, but you don't know that crying is also a form of human etiquette. So crying requires us to genuinely have all the necessary conditions, it cannot be faked; their achievements in this area are much better than ours, because they have already made it technical and professional." I said slowly, smoking my cigarette. Old Li shook his head silently, as if to say that my words did not satisfy him.

At this time, the crying had stopped, and a series of high-heeled shoes clattered on the stairs, as if several feet were racing there.

"Look, their performance is over, they are going to start another new trick." I smiled at Old Li, the footsteps had entered the next room.

"Elder sister cried really well." A girl's voice. I guess it was the third child.

"Daddy ah - why didn't you take me with you -" Another voice was imitating. I think this might be the lady in the light purple cheongsam.

"Giggle..." A burst of laughter mixed with teasing and wrestling. I made a face at Old Li.

"This is not your new discovery, you don't need to be ecstatic. Actually, what you said, 'crying has been professionalized,' has long been practiced. There are even people hired to cry in Shanghai, do you know that?" He said unconvincingly. I didn't answer, the sound of cards from next door started up.

"A Jin, go downstairs and watch, call us when it's time to cry," the eldest said.

"I really can't live here anymore, I'm going to move out alone next month if you don't move," Old Li grabbed his hair in frustration.

"Old Li, don't forget that we are 'experiencing life'!" I said to him with a smile.

"Screw it, I don't need this kind of life!"

"Don't raise your voice! Second Miss's 'Su San Starts Her Journey' is on again." I waved my hand to tell him.

"Su San left Hongtong County, came to the street, and did not speak..." Before she finished singing, she was interrupted by the sound of cymbals and drums downstairs.

Alley Scene 181

— Yin Fei

The children are playing happily in the alley, several people scrambling for a small rubber ball. The sweat on their faces is quickly wiped away with the back of their hands, leaving black streaks on their faces. But they don't care at all. While wiping away sweat, they bravely rush into the battle to grab the ball.

They have no fixed rules for kicking the ball, nor do they have goals. The one who has the ball at their feet the most is the most capable. This person is also quite majestic, kicking the ball and shouting: Come and grab it, come and grab it!

So the rest of the people crowd together and work together to grab the ball. But when the ball is grabbed, that person becomes an isolated hero, and the rest of the people surround them to grab it.

They just keep grabbing and grabbing like this.

Just as they are having a great time grabbing, a voice comes from afar:

"Hey! The Grand Master is coming! Clang! Clang!"

That person is wearing a brand new blue worker's uniform, with three or four paper flags stuck in their back (that is, taken from the incense pot), and they are still chewing something in their mouth, making their speech a little vague.

"Xiao Rong! Xiao Rong!" Some people stood still, while others continued to play.

Xiao Rong walked over; he looked like a general on the stage, imitating the recitative of an actor: "I, Zhao Yun, do not kill unknown soldiers, quickly state your name!"

Seeing that no one was talking to him, he changed his tone and said, trying to strike up a conversation, "Ermao, look at these flags, Dad bought them back, and there are incense pots, and mooncakes, such a big package, and, and..."

"And fart!"

Someone blurted out. That person rushed out fiercely:

"Who said that? You don't even have a fart!"

Everyone stopped fighting for the ball. Someone jumped out:

"I said it, what about it?"

"Ermao, beat him! I have mooncakes, I'll be good to you!" He really took out a mooncake, broke it open, and gave half to Ermao.

Ermao looked at that side and then at this side, he dared not reach out to take it.

That one made a face at him, coldly making a sound from his nose: "Hmph! You dare!" He looked around, with a bit of a question mark, "We have more people!"

"I have mooncakes! I have many, many at home!"

"We don't want to eat mooncakes. We have them too." Someone said in response.

"Yes, we don't want to eat mooncakes, we have them too." Many people responded.

"You only have farts, you eat farts, eat farts! Eat farts! Yum, yum, delicious, a little dog watches me eat!"

"You are the ones who eat farts!" That one angrily threw the ball over, breaking the paper flags on their back.

Tears hung in Xiao Rong's eyes, he wanted to rush over, but he didn't dare. Finally, he said in a trembling voice: "Ermao, hit him! I'll give you mooncakes to eat later."

Ermao looked at that side and then at this side, finally opening his mouth: "Abing, why did you break his flags?"

"None of your business, have you forgotten that he called others to hit you the day before yesterday?"

That one was speechless, but still argued: "Today is all your fault, he didn't provoke you".

"Mooncakes taste good. Did you provoke him the day before yesterday?" He paused, "There's a process, one-on-one fighting, killing people is not punishable, no one is allowed to cry!"

"Okay! One-on-one fighting, whoever helps anyone is a bastard turtle."

"You pay for my flags first, I don't care"!

"Then why didn't you pay for tearing my clothes yesterday"?

"I didn't tear the clothes".

"I didn't tear the flags either, it was the ball!"

"Then you take out the ball, and let me break it too".

"Piss"！

"Ignore him, Abing, let's kick the ball."

So they started talking again.

Ermao looked at that side and then at this side, he leaned against the wall, not knowing what to do.

Xiao Rong glared at him and said, "I won't be good to you next time, eating mooncakes deceitfully"! He shamed him, pulling a face. Then, as if discovering another path: "Abing, don't be fierce, I'll tell my dad"!

The children all ignored him, having a great time playing. The moon was already hanging in the sky, round and round.

The Sagging Bed Frame 182

— Yu

"You broom star! Husband-killing star! Since you came, the family has been uneasy for a moment. Ali has been sick and in pain. Look, you've sucked him dry, not an ounce of meat left, not an ounce of meat. His flesh has been sucked away by you, look at you, as fat as a pig. You broom star! Husband-killing star!" The father-in-law angrily poked his fingertip hard toward his daughter-in-law's face. The daughter-in-law, who was not even three feet tall and had two yellow snotty noses, rolled to the ground like a watermelon.

The daughter-in-law began to cry with a "woo" sound!

The father-in-law felt for a ruler on the table, raising his brush-like eyebrows: "Hmph! You dare to cry!" It was more effective than an order in the military camp. She wiped her nose and immediately stopped crying. Only then did the father-in-law feel relieved. He turned to look at his only son Ali, lying on the camp bed. The quilt was flat, and one couldn't tell if someone was sleeping there. The head exposed at the opening of the quilt looked like something pickled in a medicinal solution bottle in a hospital, except that the two deeply sunken eyes suddenly coughed violently, spitting out white foam-like phlegm. When his father saw that there were red threads in the phlegm,

"What? Ali, are you spitting blood?" The father was anxious, so anxious that his hands and feet didn't know where to put them, he just stood there fidgeting. He glanced at his daughter-in-law standing next to the wardrobe, looking at him nonchalantly. All his resentment was nowhere to vent. He went up and slapped her face, slapping all the yellow snot in his palm. He was so angry that he grabbed her pigtail and dragged her over, slapping her again, making her stare blankly, not knowing what great crime she had committed.

"You broom star, husband-killing star! Ali is coughing so badly, don't you know to come up and help? But you're just standing there staring. Are you cursing him to die? If he dies, I'll never let you broom star live to go to someone else. You little demon that can't be beaten to death!" With that, he slapped her again, knocking her to the ground.

Ali looked at his father hitting someone, as if he was already used to it. He coughed for a while and calmed down. His eyelids covered his eyes. The father looked at his sleeping son. He kicked his daughter-in-law, who had fallen to the ground like a snail, and wearily lay down on the bed.

In this small courtyard, there was only the dim kerosene lamp accompanying the daughter-in-law on the ground.

"Dad! Dad!" Ali suddenly opened his eyes. "The bed frame is too loose, it hurts my spine."

"Tell A Xiang to hold up the bed frame for you," the father sat up. "A Xiang, you crawl under Ali's bed and hold up the bed frame for him, go, hurry up!"

A Xiang looked at her father-in-law's blazing eyes and dejectedly crawled under Ali's bed.

Only then did the father feel at ease and go to sleep, asking, "How is it now?" His son did not answer him.

The alarm clock on the table rang loudly. But the snoring was louder than it.

"Dad! Dad!" Ali jumped out of bed as if he were crazy: "Dad! Get up, there's a ghost under my bed... a ghost is calling啊!"

The father was also so frightened that he jumped up. The faces of the father and son were all as white as paper. They trembled, sure enough, there was a sound under the bed. Ali clung to his father's waist. The father mustered up his courage, took a "copper coin sword" from the

Page 19

hook, and took a kerosene lamp, using the sword to open a piece of cloth in front of the bed and looked, there was something there. But when he brought the kerosene lamp closer, it was nothing else but his daughter-in-law sleeping there. He was furious. He dragged her out from under the bed at once. Picking up the ruler, he beat her head and face in a frenzy, without asking why.

"You broom star, husband-killing bone, you want to scare Ali to death吗"……"

A frenzy of beating. He stopped his hand when his arm was sore. A frenzy of scolding. He stopped his mouth when he was tired of scolding.

"You are not allowed to sleep tonight, kneel for me all night. The daughter-in-law knelt down, imitating a wooden chicken, touching the scars all over her face. Only then did the father take his son and sleep on his own bed.

The next day. Ali wanted water to wash his face. His father looked high and low for his daughter-in-law and couldn't find her.

"Go to Nature"

Shanghai Grand Theatre Premieres Soviet Film "Ice and Snow" 188

"The Daringo Even," a Soviet Linfei Film Company production, premiered today at the Shanghai Grand Theatre on North Sichuan Road.

The story in the film tells about seven Soviet youths who organize an Arctic expedition to Happy Bay in the Arctic Ocean for geological research. Before their departure, the village chief of the Arctic indigenous people was wounded by a polar bear, so they asked them to rescue him. The team leader, Neterenkov, ordered two people to help, and then set off for investigation with another person, while the remaining three stayed in the camp for mutual comfort. After they left, they encountered wind and rain on the way, and became half lost. The people staying in the camp saw that Liu and the other two had not returned for a long time, so they took a plane to search for their tracks. Unfortunately, the plane collided with an iceberg, and they returned without results. The next day, Liu and the other two were still missing. They set off again to search. On the way, Liu and the other two were lost in the wind for too long, and they were exhausted and dying. Just in the nick of time, the Arctic indigenous people tracked them down, and one of those who set off with Liu had died.

The plot of the whole film is unique, tense and intense, and the director's technique is also very smooth. The actions of each actor can create excellent scenes without the audience noticing; the scenery is also completely real-life shooting, extremely realistic. The distribution of actors is appropriate, it is indeed a film worth watching.
